Unlike web and mobile wallets, a hardware wallet can't be hacked without having access to the device itself, meaning there's one less way that your funds can be stolen.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe \u003ca href=\"https://shop.ledger.com/products/ledger-nano-s\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLedger Nano S\u003c/a\u003e is one of the best-known crypto hardware wallets, having sold well over a million units worldwide. But does it still cut it in 2021?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eWhat is the Ledger Nano S?\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAt $59, the Ledger Nano S is one of the cheaper hardware wallets on the market. It supports more than 1,100 cryptocurrencies, and has a sleek design and simple user interface.\u003cbr /\u003e\n\u003ciframe title=\"Ledger Nano S  Overview\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/RQkZKm_ekwM?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBut it's coming up for its fifth birthday in 2021an eternity in tech hardware termsand it's since been superseded by its feature-packed sibling, the \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/16035/ledger-nano-x-review-an-expensive-step-in-the-right-direction\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLedger Nano X\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSo is it worth shelling out for the extra bells and whistles, or does the simpler, cheaper option still have what it takes? We've taken a detailed look at the setup process and what its like to use the wallet.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Nano S: Design and build\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Ledger Nano S isn't going to win any design awards, but neither does it have the clunky aesthetic of rival hardware wallets like the Trezor One.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\"Discreet\" is probably the best word to describe it; indeed, if it weren't for the Ledger branding etched on its aluminum shield, you could easily mistake it for an oldif slightly chunkyUSB flash drive.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eRotate it open, however, and some differences immediately become apparent: there's a (tiny) screen, a micro-USB socket and two buttons atop the device for navigating its menus.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_60341\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-60341\" style=\"width: 300px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-medium wp-image-60341\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/ledger-nano-s-review-300x225.jpg\" alt=\"Ledger Nano S\" width=\"300\" height=\"225\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/ledger-nano-s-review-300x225.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/ledger-nano-s-review-768x576.jpg 768w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/ledger-nano-s-review.jpg 1280w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-60341\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eThe Ledger Nano S is available in a variety of different colors. Image: Decrypt\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Nano S is available in a variety of colorways, including green, pink, and a rather fetching transparent model. As well as letting you coordinate your Ledger with your wardrobe and interior decor, it's also handy for distinguishing between main and backup devices (or, if you're a crypto high roller who wants to split up their holdings, between different accounts).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Nano S: What's in the box?\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Nano S packaging is simple, minimalist, and clearly draws inspiration from Apple's designs. Unlike some manufacturers, Ledger doesn't bother with an anti-tamper sealit argues that the seals are \u003ca href=\"https://support.ledger.com/hc/en-us/articles/360002481534-Check-if-device-is-genuine\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eeasy to counterfeit\u003c/a\u003e and can be misleading.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_6919\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-6919\" style=\"width: 640px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-6919\" src=\"https://wp.decryptmedia.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/img_20190502_1417281-1024x576.jpg\" alt=\"We review the Ledger Nano S to see if it deserves to be one of the top ranking crypto hardware wallets.\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/img_20190502_1417281-1024x576.jpg 1024w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/img_20190502_1417281-300x169.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/img_20190502_1417281-768x432.jpg 768w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/img_20190502_1417281-2048x1152.jpg 2048w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/img_20190502_1417281.jpg 1421w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-6919\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eThe Ledger Nano S has an Apple-esque vibe. Photo Credit: Decrypt\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eInside the box, you'll find the Nano S device itself, along with a quick start guide, three cards for recording your recovery phrase, a micro-USB cable, a lanyard, and a loop for attaching your Nano S to a keyring.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cb\u003eLedger Nano S: Getting started\u003c/b\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo set up the Ledger Nano S, you'll first need to download and install the \u003ca href=\"https://www.ledger.com/ledger-live\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLedger Live\u003c/a\u003e application; upon launch, you'll need to set up a password.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOnce you've done that, connect your Ledger to your computer using the supplied micro-USB cable, and follow the on-screen prompts to set up your device.Most of the next steps are made on the device itself, and are (initially) straightforwardthe only thing you'll need to do is set up a PIN.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo navigate through the menus, use the two buttons on top of the device;click the right button to go right/up, the left button to go left/down and both buttons to select a menu item or respond to a prompt.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_6918\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-6918\" style=\"width: 640px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-6918\" src=\"https://wp.decryptmedia.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/img_20190502_141925-1024x576.jpg\" alt=\"We review the Ledger Nano S to see if it deserves to be one of the top ranking crypto hardware wallets.\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/img_20190502_141925-1024x576.jpg 1024w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/img_20190502_141925-300x169.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/img_20190502_141925-768x432.jpg 768w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/img_20190502_141925-2048x1152.jpg 2048w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/img_20190502_141925.jpg 1421w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 640px) 100vw, 640px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-6918\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eThe Ledger hardware wallet makes great use of just two buttons and a small screen. Image: Decrypt\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe next step is a little more arduous. The Ledger generates a 24-word secret phrase, which you'll need to record on one of the cards supplied with the device. That means clicking through to each word, copying it down, double-checking to make sure it's accurate, and then re-entering the words to confirm that you've recorded them correctly.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIt's a tedious process, but necessary; in a very real sense, the 24-word phrase \u003cem\u003eis\u003c/em\u003e your wallet, and the Ledger simply provides a portal through which you access it. If you lose your Ledger device (or forget your PIN number), you can enter the recovery phrase on a new Ledger, and still have access to your crypto assets. If you lose your recovery phrase, you're stuffed.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=19326 data-post-title=\"Best Crypto Wallet: Overview of the 9 Best Hardware Wallets (2020)\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/19326/best-cryptocurrency-hardware-wallets/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eBest Crypto Wallet: Overview of the 9 Best Hardware Wallets (2020)\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSome wallets require you to enter your secret phrase into an app, which then sends it to the devicemeaning the hardware wallet is pointless if your phone is hacked or stolen. By keeping the secret phrase airlocked and only held on the Ledger device, security is maximized.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThat also means you need to keep your recovery phrase\u003cem\u003every\u003c/em\u003e secure. Some Ledger users have resorted to recording their 24 words in a metal wallet (card, after all, can be burned or disintegrate in water), or splitting their recovery phrase up and storing it in multiple locations.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOnce you've chosen a PIN and recorded your recovery phrase, you'll need to verify your device through the Ledger Live app, which should take just a few seconds.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Live\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Ledger Live software is, for most users, the main way you'll interact with your Ledger Nano S. Fortunately, it's a beautiful, streamlined app that is very easy to use.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUnlike the Nano X, which has Bluetooth connectivity and an internal battery, you'll need to connect the Nano S to your computer via a micro-USB cable in order to use Ledger Live. You can also use the Nano S with Ledger Live's \u003ca href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.ledger.live\u0026amp;hl=en_GB\u0026amp;gl=US\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eAndroid mobile app\u003c/a\u003e, using the \u003ca href=\"https://shop.ledger.com/products/ledger-otg-kit\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLedger OTG kit\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eEach time you plug the device in, you'll need to enter your PIN code.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe first thing you'll need to do on launching is to add some apps to your Ledger. To do this, navigate to \"settings\" in the left-hand column of Ledger Live. You'll be prompted to \"allow Ledger Manager\" on your device. Here you can check whether your device has the latest firmware (and update it if necessary), and add or update apps.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ciframe title=\"Ledger Nano S  Install / Uninstall Applications\" width=\"640\" height=\"480\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/5keXdbhLfuY?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eApps essentially represent cryptocurrency coins or tokens; Bitcoin, Ethereum, Cosmos and so forth. When you install the relevant app, you'll need to add an account; this will then show up in the \"portfolio\" section of Ledger Live.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOnce you've installed your apps, you can send and receive crypto. To receive, you can either navigate to the \"Accounts\" section and pick whichever account you want to use, or use the \"send\" and \"receive\" buttons in the sidebar and select your chosen cryptocurrency from the drop-down menu.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou'll also need to open the app for the relevant cryptocurrency on your Nano S device.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ciframe title=\"Ledger Nano S  Receiving Assets\" width=\"640\" height=\"480\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/-IwdZUrqsi4?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo send or receive, you'll need to confirm the sending or receiving address on your Ledger Nano S. This can be a fiddly business; it involves checking the address in Ledger Live against the characters on the Ledger's tiny screen (which is so small it can't render the entire address on one screen, forcing you to click through to see the whole thing).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThat's the most painful part of the process, though; once you've done that, it's plain sailing. Sending and receiving crypto is a smooth process; Ledger Live also offers options for buying and selling certain cryptocurrencies directly in the app.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Nano S: ease of use and features\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou're not just limited to using the Nano S with Ledger Live, however. The hardware wallet can also be used in conjunction with web wallets, such as \u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"MetaMask review\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/50431/metamask-crypto-wallet-review\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eMetaMask\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e, MyEtherWallet, and MyCrypto.\u003cbr /\u003e\n\u003ciframe title=\"Ledger Nano X  Protect your accounts with Fido U2F\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/KPmf9mbYKuo?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYou can also use the Nano S as a security key for \u003ca href=\"https://www.ledger.com/fido-u2f\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003etwo-factor authentication\u003c/a\u003e, by installing the FIDO U2F app. This enables you to verify your login credentials using your hardware wallet on a number of different web services, including \u003ca href=\"https://myaccount.google.com/signinoptions/two-step-verification/enroll-welcome\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eGoogle\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"https://www.facebook.com/help/401566786855239\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eFacebook\u003c/a\u003e, \u003ca href=\"https://help.github.com/articles/configuring-two-factor-authentication-via-fido-u2f/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eGitHub\u003c/a\u003e and \u003ca href=\"https://www.dropbox.com/fr/help/363\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eDropbox\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ciframe title=\"Ledger Nano S - The Recovery Check App\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/p1gEYrYMo7Y?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThere's also a recovery check app, which enables you to check that you've recorded your recovery phrase accurately without requiring you to reset your Ledger.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Nano S: supported assets\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Ledger Nano S supports over 1,100 crypto assets, 29 of which you can manage directly using Ledger Live. Some of the coins and tokens available include:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"bitcoin news\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/crypto-news/bitcoin\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eBitcoin\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e (BTC)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"More about Ethereum\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/crypto-news/ethereum\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eEthereum\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e (ETH) and \u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"What are ERC20 tokens?\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/erc20\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eERC20\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e tokens\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca (BCH)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"More about Litecoin\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/crypto-news/litecoin\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLitecoin\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e (LTC)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"More about Tether\" (DOT)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eHowever, because of the limited storage capacity of the Nano S, you'll only be able to run two or three of the relevant wallet apps on the device at any one time. If you have a diverse portfolio, you might want to consider the Nano X as an alternative, as its expanded internal memory means that it's able to store a lot more apps at once.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Nano S: Security\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eObviously the most important part of a hardware wallet is its security credentials, and Ledger hasn't skimped in that regard. Like the Nano X and Ledger Blue, the Nano S has a physically isolated secure element that's \u003ca href=\"https://www.ledger.com/academy/security/the-importance-of-certification\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eCC EAL5+ certified\u003c/a\u003ethe highest such rating available against penetration tests.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThese secure elements are similar to those used in credit cards, passports and SIM cards; in addition, Ledger uses its own proprietary operating system, \u003ca href=\"https://www.ledger.com/academy/security/our-custom-operating-system-bolos\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eBOLOS\u003c/a\u003e. This ensures that the various applications running on the Nano S, and the 24-word recovery phrase, are isolated from each other, and requires that physical confirmation for each transaction needs to take place.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Nano S and Nano X are also the only hardware wallets to receive \u003ca href=\"https://www.ledger.com/ledger-nano-x-recognized-as-certified-crypto-hardware-wallet\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eCSPN (First Level Security Certificate) certification\u003c/a\u003e, from ANSSIthe National Cybersecurity Agency of France.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhile Ledger's physical security is extremely tightmaking it one of the most secure cold storage solutions on the marketLedger the company has had some embarrassing security lapses in the past.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cblockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\"\u003e\n\u003cp lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"\u003eRecently, we shared news of a data dump. On December 23, we were alerted by our e-commerce provider Shopify about an incident in April \u0026amp; June \u0026#39;20 where their rogue team members exported merchants\u0026#39; customer databases. Ledger was included. More details: \u003ca href=\"https://t.co/NHU3IbDL0a\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ehttps://t.co/NHU3IbDL0a\u003c/a\u003e \u003ca href=\"https://t.co/DHQQ9arxCu\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003epic.twitter.com/DHQQ9arxCu\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u0026mdash; Ledger (@Ledger) \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/Ledger/status/1349375083891011591?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eJanuary 13, 2021\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cscript async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"\u003e\u003c/script\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eNotably, in June 2020, data from its e-commerce database was leaked, with \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/52118/hacked-ledger-database-dumped-on-raidforums\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eover a million customer records\u003c/a\u003e finding their way to hacker forums. As a result, some Ledger customers found themselves at the mercy of \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/54319/ledger-users-get-phishing-phone-calls-after-database-leak\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ephishing attacks\u003c/a\u003e, and even \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/52136/ledger-customers-now-getting-threatening-emails-for-bitcoin-ransoms\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ethreats\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAs a result, Ledger has committed to \u003ca href=\"https://www.ledger.com/blog/update-efforts-to-protect-your-data-and-prosecute-the-scammers\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003echanging its procedures\u003c/a\u003e for handling customer data, though it's scant comfort to those who have had their personal information (and the fact that they hold enough cryptocurrency for it to be worth securing in cold storage) exposed.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Nano S review: Verdict\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIt may be getting a bit long in the tooth, but at just $59, the Ledger Nano S is a stealeither as a backup device if you already own a Nano X, or as a cold storage solution in its own right.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=16035 data-post-title=\"Ledger Nano X Review (2021): An Expensive Step In The Right Direction\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/16035/ledger-nano-x-review-an-expensive-step-in-the-right-direction/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLedger Nano X Review (2021): An Expensive Step In The Right Direction\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIts main limitations are its storage capacity (meaning that you can only run two or three apps on it at any given time), its tiny screen, and the fact that you need to plug it into a computer to use it. All of these are addressed by the Ledger Nano X, though the extra $60 is quite a steep price increase for the upgrade.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFor most people, especially those with a small portfolio of crypto assets, the Nano S is a reliable workhorse, and all the wallet you'll need.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRating: 4/5\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"\u003cp\u003eThe Ledger Nano S is one of the best-selling crypto hardware wallets of all time. wallet","slug":"hardware-wallet","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":10360,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":23,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":9533,"name":"hardware wallets","slug":"hardware-wallets","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":9533,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":11,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":10359,"name":"ledger","slug":"ledger","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":10359,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":36,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":28869,"name":"Ledger Nano S","slug":"ledger-nano-s","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":28869,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":4,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":7672,"name":"Reviews","slug":"reviews","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":7672,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":4,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":5423,"name":"Technology","slug":"technology","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":5423,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":2103,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}}],"link":[]},"content_text":"One of the best ways to keep your cryptocurrency safe is to use a hardware walleta secure hardware device for storing your private keys. Unlike web and mobile wallets, a hardware wallet can't be hacked without having access to the device itself, meaning there's one less way that your funds can be stolen.\n\nThe Ledger Nano S is one of the best-known crypto hardware wallets, having sold well over a million units worldwide. But does it still cut it in 2021?\n\nWHAT IS THE LEDGER NANO S?\n\nAt $59, the Ledger Nano S is one of the cheaper hardware wallets on the market. It supports more than 1,100 cryptocurrencies, and has a sleek design and simple user interface.\n\nBut it's coming up for its fifth birthday in 2021an eternity in tech hardware termsand it's since been superseded by its feature-packed sibling, the Ledger Nano X.\n\nSo is it worth shelling out for the extra bells and whistles, or does the simpler, cheaper option still have what it takes? We've taken a detailed look at the setup process and what its like to use the wallet.\n\nLEDGER NANO S: DESIGN AND BUILD\n\nThe Ledger Nano S isn't going to win any design awards, but neither does it have the clunky aesthetic of rival hardware wallets like the Trezor One.\n\n\"Discreet\" is probably the best word to describe it; indeed, if it weren't for the Ledger branding etched on its aluminum shield, you could easily mistake it for an oldif slightly chunkyUSB flash drive.\n\nRotate it open, however, and some differences immediately become apparent: there's a (tiny) screen, a micro-USB socket and two buttons atop the device for navigating its menus.\n[Ledger Nano S]The Ledger Nano S is available in a variety of different colors. Image: Decrypt\nThe Nano S is available in a variety of colorways, including green, pink, and a rather fetching transparent model. As well as letting you coordinate your Ledger with your wardrobe and interior decor, it's also handy for distinguishing between main and backup devices (or, if you're a crypto high roller who wants to split up their holdings, between different accounts).\n\nLEDGER NANO S: WHAT'S IN THE BOX?\n\nThe Nano S packaging is simple, minimalist, and clearly draws inspiration from Apple's designs. Unlike some manufacturers, Ledger doesn't bother with an anti-tamper sealit argues that the seals are easy to counterfeit and can be misleading.\n[We review the Ledger Nano S to see if it deserves to be one of the top ranking crypto hardware wallets.]The Ledger Nano S has an Apple-esque vibe. Photo Credit: Decrypt\nInside the box, you'll find the Nano S device itself, along with a quick start guide, three cards for recording your recovery phrase, a micro-USB cable, a lanyard, and a loop for attaching your Nano S to a keyring.\n\nLEDGER NANO S: GETTING STARTED\n\nTo set up the Ledger Nano S, you'll first need to download and install the Ledger Live application; upon launch, you'll need to set up a password.\n\nOnce you've done that, connect your Ledger to your computer using the supplied micro-USB cable, and follow the on-screen prompts to set up your device.Most of the next steps are made on the device itself, and are (initially) straightforwardthe only thing you'll need to do is set up a PIN.\n\nTo navigate through the menus, use the two buttons on top of the device;click the right button to go right/up, the left button to go left/down and both buttons to select a menu item or respond to a prompt.\n[We review the Ledger Nano S to see if it deserves to be one of the top ranking crypto hardware wallets.]The Ledger hardware wallet makes great use of just two buttons and a small screen. Image: Decrypt\nThe next step is a little more arduous. The Ledger generates a 24-word secret phrase, which you'll need to record on one of the cards supplied with the device. That means clicking through to each word, copying it down, double-checking to make sure it's accurate, and then re-entering the words to confirm that you've recorded them correctly.\n\nIt's a tedious process, but necessary; in a very real sense, the 24-word phrase _is_ your wallet, and the Ledger simply provides a portal through which you access it. If you lose your Ledger device (or forget your PIN number), you can enter the recovery phrase on a new Ledger, and still have access to your crypto assets. If you lose your recovery phrase, you're stuffed.\n\nBest Crypto Wallet: Overview of the 9 Best Hardware Wallets (2020)\nSome wallets require you to enter your secret phrase into an app, which then sends it to the devicemeaning the hardware wallet is pointless if your phone is hacked or stolen. By keeping the secret phrase airlocked and only held on the Ledger device, security is maximized.\n\nThat also means you need to keep your recovery phrase_very_ secure. Some Ledger users have resorted to recording their 24 words in a metal wallet (card, after all, can be burned or disintegrate in water), or splitting their recovery phrase up and storing it in multiple locations.\n\nOnce you've chosen a PIN and recorded your recovery phrase, you'll need to verify your device through the Ledger Live app, which should take just a few seconds.\n\nLEDGER LIVE\n\nThe Ledger Live software is, for most users, the main way you'll interact with your Ledger Nano S. Fortunately, it's a beautiful, streamlined app that is very easy to use.\n\nUnlike the Nano X, which has Bluetooth connectivity and an internal battery, you'll need to connect the Nano S to your computer via a micro-USB cable in order to use Ledger Live. You can also use the Nano S with Ledger Live's Android mobile app, using the Ledger OTG kit.\n\nEach time you plug the device in, you'll need to enter your PIN code.\n\nThe first thing you'll need to do on launching is to add some apps to your Ledger. To do this, navigate to \"settings\" in the left-hand column of Ledger Live. You'll be prompted to \"allow Ledger Manager\" on your device. Here you can check whether your device has the latest firmware (and update it if necessary), and add or update apps.\n\nApps essentially represent cryptocurrency coins or tokens; Bitcoin, Ethereum, Cosmos and so forth. When you install the relevant app, you'll need to add an account; this will then show up in the \"portfolio\" section of Ledger Live.\n\nOnce you've installed your apps, you can send and receive crypto. To receive, you can either navigate to the \"Accounts\" section and pick whichever account you want to use, or use the \"send\" and \"receive\" buttons in the sidebar and select your chosen cryptocurrency from the drop-down menu.\n\nYou'll also need to open the app for the relevant cryptocurrency on your Nano S device.\n\nTo send or receive, you'll need to confirm the sending or receiving address on your Ledger Nano S. This can be a fiddly business; it involves checking the address in Ledger Live against the characters on the Ledger's tiny screen (which is so small it can't render the entire address on one screen, forcing you to click through to see the whole thing).\n\nThat's the most painful part of the process, though; once you've done that, it's plain sailing. Sending and receiving crypto is a smooth process; Ledger Live also offers options for buying and selling certain cryptocurrencies directly in the app.\n\nLEDGER NANO S: EASE OF USE AND FEATURES\n\nYou're not just limited to using the Nano S with Ledger Live, however. The hardware wallet can also be used in conjunction with web wallets, such as MetaMask, MyEtherWallet, and MyCrypto.\n\nYou can also use the Nano S as a security key for two-factor authentication, by installing the FIDO U2F app. This enables you to verify your login credentials using your hardware wallet on a number of different web services, including Google, Facebook, GitHub and Dropbox.\n\nThere's also a recovery check app, which enables you to check that you've recorded your recovery phrase accurately without requiring you to reset your Ledger.\n\nLEDGER NANO S: SUPPORTED ASSETS\n\nThe Ledger Nano S supports over 1,100 crypto assets, 29 of which you can manage directly using Ledger Live. Some of the coins and tokens available include:\n\n \t* Bitcoin (BTC)\n \t* Ethereum (ETH) and ERC20 tokens\n \t* XRP\n \t* Bitcoin Cash (BCH)\n \t* Litecoin (LTC)\n \t* Tether (USDT)\n \t* Binance Coin (BNB)\n \t* EOS\n \t* Stellar (XLM)\n \t* Cardano (ADA)\n \t* Monero (XMR)\n \t* Cosmos (ATOM)\n \t* Polkadot (DOT)\n\nHowever, because of the limited storage capacity of the Nano S, you'll only be able to run two or three of the relevant wallet apps on the device at any one time. If you have a diverse portfolio, you might want to consider the Nano X as an alternative, as its expanded internal memory means that it's able to store a lot more apps at once.\n\nLEDGER NANO S: SECURITY\n\nObviously the most important part of a hardware wallet is its security credentials, and Ledger hasn't skimped in that regard. Like the Nano X and Ledger Blue, the Nano S has a physically isolated secure element that's CC EAL5+ certifiedthe highest such rating available against penetration tests.\n\nThese secure elements are similar to those used in credit cards, passports and SIM cards; in addition, Ledger uses its own proprietary operating system, BOLOS. This ensures that the various applications running on the Nano S, and the 24-word recovery phrase, are isolated from each other, and requires that physical confirmation for each transaction needs to take place.\n\nThe Nano S and Nano X are also the only hardware wallets to receive CSPN (First Level Security Certificate) certification, from ANSSIthe National Cybersecurity Agency of France.\n\nWhile Ledger's physical security is extremely tightmaking it one of the most secure cold storage solutions on the marketLedger the company has had some embarrassing security lapses in the past.\n\n\u003eRecently,wesharednewsofadatadump.OnDecember23,wewerealertedbyoure-commerceproviderShopifyaboutanincidentinApril\u0026June'20wheretheirrogueteammembersexportedmerchants'customerdatabases.Ledgerwasincluded.Moredetails:https://t.co/NHU3IbDL0apic.twitter.com/DHQQ9arxCu\n\u003e\n\u003eLedger(@Ledger)January13,2021\n\nNotably, in June 2020, data from its e-commerce database was leaked, with over a million customer records finding their way to hacker forums. As a result, some Ledger customers found themselves at the mercy of phishing attacks, and even threats.\n\nAs a result, Ledger has committed to changing its procedures for handling customer data, though it's scant comfort to those who have had their personal information (and the fact that they hold enough cryptocurrency for it to be worth securing in cold storage) exposed.\n\nLEDGER NANO S REVIEW: VERDICT\n\nIt may be getting a bit long in the tooth, but at just $59, the Ledger Nano S is a stealeither as a backup device if you already own a Nano X, or as a cold storage solution in its own right.\n\nLedger Nano X Review (2021): An Expensive Step In The Right Direction\nIts main limitations are its storage capacity (meaning that you can only run two or three apps on it at any given time), its tiny screen, and the fact that you need to plug it into a computer to use it. All of these are addressed by the Ledger Nano X, though the extra $60 is quite a steep price increase for the upgrade.\n\nFor most people, especially those with a small portfolio of crypto assets, the Nano S is a reliable workhorse, and all the wallet you'll need.\n\nRATING: 4/5\n","read_this_next_post_id":"6907","read_this_next_post_type":"post","social_share_img_url":"https://cdn.decrypt.co/resize/1024/height/512/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/ledger-nano-s-review-main-2-gID_7.jpg","featured_image_caption":"The Ledger Nano S hardware wallet. Image: Decrypt","featured_image_description":"The Ledger Nano S hardware wallet. Nano X Review (2021): An Expensive Step In The Right Direction"},"content":{"rendered":"\u003cp\u003eSince cryptocurrencies were invented over a decade ago, there have been many attempts to build more advanced, secure and user-friendly \u003cspan class=\"definition\" link=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/?post_type=post\u0026p=5702\" slug=\"wallet\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/?post_type=post\u0026amp;p=5702\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ewallets\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003eto store them.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAs of 2021, the current gold standard for security is known as a hardware walleta physical device that stores your cryptocurrency private keys in a secure offline environment.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOne of the most prominent companies involved in moving the needle forward is \u003ca href=\"https://www.ledger.com/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLedger\u003c/a\u003e, the firm behind the popular, but flawed \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/6915/ledger-nano-decrypt-review\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLedger Nano S\u003c/a\u003e hardware walletand the Ledger Nano X, its flagship device.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWith a bigger screen, Bluetooth connectivity and a built-in battery, the Nano X is certainly an upgradebut does it live up to the hype? Let's find out.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Nano X review: Design and build\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_16287\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-16287\" style=\"width: 1280px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-16287 size-full\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER6-e1578609273277.jpg\" alt=\"Ledger Nano X review: design and build\" width=\"1280\" height=\"720\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER6-e1578609273277.jpg 1280w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER6-e1578609273277-300x169.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER6-e1578609273277-1024x576.jpg 1024w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER6-e1578609273277-768x432.jpg 768w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER6-e1578609273277-2048x1152.jpg 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1280px) 100vw, 1280px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-16287\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eThe Ledger Nano X is twice the sizeand weightof the Nano S (Image: Decrypt)\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAt 72mm x 18.6mm x 11.75mm with a weight of 34g, the Ledger Nano X is almost twice as large and more than twice as heavy as the Ledger Nano S.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOne reason for the Nano X's greater bulk is that it has a built-in 100mAH battery, meaning that you can use it on the moveunlike its predecessor, which had to be plugged into a PC using a USB cable to draw power. Also filling out its frame are increased memory and a larger OLED screen.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAs we can see, although the Ledger Nano X is far smaller than the KeepKey wallet and the Ledger Blue, it is noticeably larger than the Nano S and Trezor Model One. Nonetheless, it is still an incredibly small device, and is roughly comparable in size to a common USB pen drive.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOverall, the Ledger Nano X has a modern aesthetic that is similar to the Ledger Nano S, albeit more streamlined, since the buttons are now built into the body of the device and sit flush with the casing.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_16293\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-16293\" style=\"width: 1267px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-16293 size-full\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER4-e1578609652173.jpg\" alt=\"Ledger Nano X review: size comparison\" width=\"1267\" height=\"713\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER4-e1578609652173.jpg 1267w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER4-e1578609652173-300x169.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER4-e1578609652173-1024x576.jpg 1024w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER4-e1578609652173-768x432.jpg 768w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER4-e1578609652173-2048x1152.jpg 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1267px) 100vw, 1267px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-16293\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eThe Ledger Nano X may be hefty, but it's comparable to other wallets (Image: Decrypt)\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Nano X review: What's in the box?\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Ledger Nano X comes supplied in a small cellophane-wrapped box, measuring approximately 80mm x 131mm x 31mm. Interestingly, Ledger chooses not to use tamper-evident seals on its packaging, \u003ca href=\"https://support.ledger.com/hc/en-us/articles/360002481534-Check-if-device-is-genuine\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003estating that\u003c/a\u003e they're \"easy to counterfeit and can therefore be misleading.\"\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eInside the box, you'll find the Ledger Nano X device (obviously), in addition to a braided USB A to USB C cable and a keychain strap. Documentation includes a getting started leaflet, three recovery sheets (for recording recovery phrases) as well as several stickers featuring Ledger branding.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Nano X review: Ease of use\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_16284\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-16284\" style=\"width: 1280px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-16284 size-full\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER1-e1578609412939.jpg\" alt=\"Ledger Nano X review: ease of use\" width=\"1280\" height=\"720\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER1-e1578609412939.jpg 1280w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER1-e1578609412939-300x169.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER1-e1578609412939-1024x576.jpg 1024w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER1-e1578609412939-768x432.jpg 768w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER1-e1578609412939-2048x1152.jpg 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1280px) 100vw, 1280px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-16284\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eThe Ledger Nano X's large screen and controls make it easier to use (Image: Decrypt)\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Nano X may be heftier than the Nano S, but it's still a small device. As a result, navigating through the on-device menu isn't exactly the simplest process in the worldparticularly when considering the fact that it only has two buttons. However, the larger screen and controls make for a significantly less fiddly user experience than that of the Ledger Nano S.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eNavigating the device's menu involves scrolling left or right using the left and right button respectively, or selecting options by pressing both buttons simultaneously. Beyond this, most of the action actually occurs on the associated \u003ca href=\"https://www.ledger.com/ledger-live/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLedger Live\u003c/a\u003e application, with the Ledger device itself being mostly used for verifying addresses and authorizing transactions.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Ledger Nano X's larger screen resolves one of the most common gripes about the Nano S, since crypto addresses can now be displayed in their entirety instead of requiring you to scroll. One niggling issue is that the Nano X ships with a relatively short USB cablejust 50cm long, which can make it difficult to use if your computer isn't in a convenient location.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Nano X review: Getting Started\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_16296\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-16296\" style=\"width: 1004px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-16296 size-full\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/Screenshot-2020-01-09-at-22.42.17-e1578612895963.png\" alt=\"Ledger Live\" width=\"1004\" height=\"565\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/Screenshot-2020-01-09-at-22.42.17-e1578612895963.png 1004w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/Screenshot-2020-01-09-at-22.42.17-e1578612895963-300x169.png 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/Screenshot-2020-01-09-at-22.42.17-e1578612895963-768x432.png 768w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/Screenshot-2020-01-09-at-22.42.17-e1578612895963-2048x1152.png 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1004px) 100vw, 1004px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-16296\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eTo get started, you'll need to use the Ledger Live app (Image: Ledger)\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTo begin using the device, you'll first need to download and install the \u003ca href=\"https://www.ledger.com/ledger-live/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLedger Live\u003c/a\u003e client for your operating system. This is currently available for most desktop operating systems including Windows, Mac OS, Linux, as well as mobile operating systems like iOS and Android.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOnce Ledger Live is up and running, you can power up the Ledger Nano X device by holding the left button, after which you'll be able to navigate through the startup screens to configure the device.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ciframe title=\"Ledger Nano X  Configure a new device\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/ZF4W3xgOUhQ?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThis will involve choosing a 4 to 8 digit PIN code, and backing up and verifying the randomly generated 24-word recovery phrase shown on the device. Overall, this process takes around 5 to 10 minutes, and only needs to be completed once.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBy default, the device doesn't ship with any preinstalled wallet apps. Instead, these need to be manually downloaded by connecting the Ledger Nano X with Ledger Live. Thanks to its Bluetooth capabilities, the Ledger Nano X is able to pair with mobile devices running Ledger Live wirelessly; if you're using the device with a desktop PC, you'll have to use the supplied USB cable.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Nano X review: Features\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_16299\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-16299\" style=\"width: 1152px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-16299 size-full\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER10-e1578610503888.jpg\" alt=\"Ledger Nano X review: apps\" width=\"1152\" height=\"646\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER10-e1578610503888.jpg 1152w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER10-e1578610503888-300x168.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER10-e1578610503888-1024x574.jpg 1024w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER10-e1578610503888-768x431.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1152px) 100vw, 1152px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-16299\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eThe Ledger Nano X can store up to 100 apps simultaneously (Image: Decrypt)\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAs a hardware wallet, the Ledger Nano X is primarily designed for the safe storage of cryptocurrencies and other crypto assets. Because of this, the Ledger Nano X is compatible with practically every major cryptoasset, while support for new assets is added regularly.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Ledger Nano X also overcomes one of the major limitations of its Ledger Nano S, by bumping the available internal memory from 320kb up to 2048kb. This allows users to store up to 100 apps on their device at onceconsiderably more than the 3 to 7 simultaneous apps the Ledger Nano S could hold. This means the Ledger Nano X can currently hold the entire app library simultaneouslyavoiding the need to manually remove and switch out apps due to memory constraints.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhile the vast majority of these apps allow the wallet to hold additional cryptocurrencies and tokens, a handful impart additional functionality to the Nano X. For example, the FIDO U2F app turns the device into a two-factor authentication key, whereas the recovery check app can be used to ensure you have correctly saved your recovery phrase.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=6915 data-post-title=\"Ledger Nano S Review (2021): Still The Best Hardware Wallet?\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/6915/ledger-nano-s-review/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLedger Nano S Review (2021): Still The Best Hardware Wallet?\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMoreover, the Ledger Nano X is the first cryptocurrency hardware wallet to include a built-in 100mAH battery, a necessary upgrade since the device now features Bluetooth connectivity out of the box. This allows the device to connect to mobile devices wirelessly, whereas the older Ledger Nano S could only connect to mobile devices using a \u003ca href=\"https://shop.ledger.com/products/ledger-otg-kit\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLedger OTG Kit\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWith the addition of wireless connectivity, increased memory, and a much larger screen, Ledger has clearly paid attention to the shortcomings of its earlier products and is trying to make safely storing crypto assets a less challenging task.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Nano X review: Supported crypto assets\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_16311\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-16311\" style=\"width: 1188px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-16311 size-full\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/Screenshot-2020-01-09-at-23.02.36.png\" alt=\"Ledger apps\" width=\"1188\" height=\"602\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/Screenshot-2020-01-09-at-23.02.36.png 1188w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/Screenshot-2020-01-09-at-23.02.36-300x152.png 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/Screenshot-2020-01-09-at-23.02.36-1024x519.png 1024w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/Screenshot-2020-01-09-at-23.02.36-768x389.png 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1188px) 100vw, 1188px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-16311\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eThe Ledger Nano X can store over 1,000 crypto assets (Image: Ledger)\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Ledger Nano X is compatible with well over 1,000 digital assets, including 23 coins and all ERC-20 tokens. Many of these can be managed through Ledger Live, whereas some require the Ledger Nano X to be used in conjunction with a compatible wallet. Supported crypto assets include;\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"bitcoin news\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/crypto-news/bitcoin\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eBitcoin\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e (BTC)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"More about Ethereum\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/crypto-news/ethereum\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eEthereum\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e (ETH) and \u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"What are ERC20 tokens?\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/erc20\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eERC20\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e tokens\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"All our news about XRP\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/crypto-news/xrp\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eXRP\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eEOS\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"More about Stellar\" alt=\"More about Cardano\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/crypto-news/cardano\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eCardano\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e (ADA)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eCosmos\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e (ATOM)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"More about Polkadot\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/what-is-polkadot-how-to-buy-it\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ePolkadot\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e (DOT)\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eand over 1,000 more\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Ledger Nano X supports practically every crypto asset supported by the Ledger Nano S, but is able to hold more of the relevant wallet apps at any one time thanks to its expanded internal memory.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAs such, the Ledger Nano X is ideal for securing diverse portfolios, though individuals looking to store newly released crypto assets may need to wait until Ledger adds support for them.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Nano X review: Security\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_16308\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-16308\" style=\"width: 1280px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-16308 size-full\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER9-e1578610976465.jpg\" alt=\"Ledger Nano X review: Security\" width=\"1280\" height=\"720\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER9-e1578610976465.jpg 1280w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER9-e1578610976465-300x169.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER9-e1578610976465-1024x576.jpg 1024w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER9-e1578610976465-768x432.jpg 768w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/LEDGER9-e1578610976465-2048x1152.jpg 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1280px) 100vw, 1280px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-16308\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eThe Ledger Nano X incorporates security features including a CC EAL5+ physically isolated security element (Image: Decrypt)\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAs a hardware wallet, the Ledger Nano X targets the minority of cryptocurrency users that value security above all else. As such, the team behind the product has clearly put a great deal of thought into the potential ways such a device could be attacked, and have incorporated a huge number of potential safeguards into its design.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eLike all Ledger devices, the Nano X features state-of-the-art security and incorporates a physically isolated security element certified as CC EAL5+. These secure elements are similar to those used to secure credit and debit cards, and are the standard used by banks for the protection of financial information.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe device also features a dual-core MCU which runs a proprietary operating system known as BOLOS and controls communication between the connected device and the Ledger secure element.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAlthough the addition of Bluetooth theoretically increases the number of potential entry points hackers could use to compromise the device, the Ledger Nano X encrypts Bluetooth traffic between the mobile device and requires manual verification for all important device actions.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ciframe title=\"A Closer Look At The Ledger Nano X\" width=\"640\" height=\"480\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/NGIjVKY-hvk?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBeyond this, Ledger's Nano X and Nano S are the only hardware wallets to receive \u003ca href=\"https://www.ledger.com/ledger-nano-x-recognized-as-certified-crypto-hardware-wallet\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eCSPN (First Level Security Certificate) certification\u003c/a\u003e, which means their security has been independently certified by ANSSIthe National Cybersecurity Agency of France.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThese hardware-based security measures are also supplemented with several software-based ones, including a 4-8 digital security PIN, automatic inactivity lockouts and an optional Ledger Live password lock.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOverall, the Ledger Nano X is without question one of the most secure cold storage solutions on the market.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eHowever, although its devices offer a high level of security, Ledger has experienced some security lapses as a company.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn June 2020, data from the company's e-commerce database was leaked, resulting in \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/52118/hacked-ledger-database-dumped-on-raidforums\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eover a million customer records\u003c/a\u003e being posted to hacker forums. Some quarter of a million records included details such as physical addresses and phone numbersexposing Ledger customers to the threat of \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/54319/ledger-users-get-phishing-phone-calls-after-database-leak\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ephishing attacks\u003c/a\u003e and even \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/52136/ledger-customers-now-getting-threatening-emails-for-bitcoin-ransoms\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ethreats\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cblockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\"\u003e\n\u003cp lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"\u003eRecently, we shared news of a data dump. On December 23, we were alerted by our e-commerce provider Shopify about an incident in April \u0026amp; June \u0026#39;20 where their rogue team members exported merchants\u0026#39; customer databases. Ledger was included. More details: \u003ca href=\"https://t.co/NHU3IbDL0a\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ehttps://t.co/NHU3IbDL0a\u003c/a\u003e \u003ca href=\"https://t.co/DHQQ9arxCu\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003epic.twitter.com/DHQQ9arxCu\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u0026mdash; Ledger (@Ledger) \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/Ledger/status/1349375083891011591?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eJanuary 13, 2021\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cscript async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"\u003e\u003c/script\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhile Ledger has \u003ca href=\"https://www.ledger.com/blog/update-efforts-to-protect-your-data-and-prosecute-the-scammers\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ecommitted\u003c/a\u003e to changing how it handles customer data and identifying and prosecuting those responsible, it's an embarrassing lapse for a company whose business is the security of your crypto.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eLedger Nano X review: Verdict\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe \u003ca href=\"https://shop.ledger.com/products/ledger-nano-x\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLedger Nano X\u003c/a\u003e is currently available for purchase from the \u003ca href=\"https://shop.ledger.com/pages/retailers\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eofficial Ledger website\u003c/a\u003e for $119. With that said, it can often be found for cheaper at authorized third-party retailers as well as official resellers on Amazon. You should exercise caution when purchasing any hardware wallet, making sure to only purchase from authorized sources, and never using any hardware wallet that has already been configured.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAt twice the price of the Ledger Nano S, the Nano X is one of the more expensive hardware wallets on the market. If portability and usability are your top concerns, it's probably worth the hit on your walletbut if you're already happy with the Ledger Nano S, there's little reason to upgrade.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe addition of Bluetooth and massively expanded internal memory are steps in the right direction, whereas the huge range of supported cryptocurrencies means that even the most diverse cryptocurrency investors can secure their entire portfolio.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Ledger Nano X is an excellent product marred only by its high price tag; those in the market for a less expensive alternative may want to take a look at the cheaper, but dated \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/6915/ledger-nano-decrypt-review\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLedger Nano S\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cstrong\u003eRating: 4/5\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"\u003cp\u003eThe Ledger Nano X hardware wallet features Bluetooth, an OLED screen and support for over 1k crypto assets.
