wallets","slug":"hardware-wallets","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":9533,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":11,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":10359,"name":"ledger","slug":"ledger","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":10359,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":36,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":4622,"name":"review","slug":"review","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":4622,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":6,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":7672,"name":"Reviews","slug":"reviews","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":7672,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":4,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}}],"link":[]},"content_text":"Since cryptocurrencies were invented over a decade ago, there have been many attempts to build more advanced, secure and user-friendly walletsto store them.\n\nAs of 2021, the current gold standard for security is known as a hardware walleta physical device that stores your cryptocurrency private keys in a secure offline environment.\n\nOne of the most prominent companies involved in moving the needle forward is Ledger, the firm behind the popular, but flawed Ledger Nano S hardware walletand the Ledger Nano X, its flagship device.\n\nWith a bigger screen, Bluetooth connectivity and a built-in battery, the Nano X is certainly an upgradebut does it live up to the hype? Let's find out.\n\nLEDGER NANO X REVIEW: DESIGN AND BUILD\n\n [Ledger Nano X review: design and build]The Ledger Nano X is twice the sizeand weightof the Nano S (Image: Decrypt)\nAt 72mm x 18.6mm x 11.75mm with a weight of 34g, the Ledger Nano X is almost twice as large and more than twice as heavy as the Ledger Nano S.\n\nOne reason for the Nano X's greater bulk is that it has a built-in 100mAH battery, meaning that you can use it on the moveunlike its predecessor, which had to be plugged into a PC using a USB cable to draw power. Also filling out its frame are increased memory and a larger OLED screen.\n\nAs we can see, although the Ledger Nano X is far smaller than the KeepKey wallet and the Ledger Blue, it is noticeably larger than the Nano S and Trezor Model One. Nonetheless, it is still an incredibly small device, and is roughly comparable in size to a common USB pen drive.\n\nOverall, the Ledger Nano X has a modern aesthetic that is similar to the Ledger Nano S, albeit more streamlined, since the buttons are now built into the body of the device and sit flush with the casing.\n[Ledger Nano X review: size comparison]The Ledger Nano X may be hefty, but it's comparable to other wallets (Image: Decrypt) \n\nLEDGER NANO X REVIEW: WHAT'S IN THE BOX?\n\nThe Ledger Nano X comes supplied in a small cellophane-wrapped box, measuring approximately 80mm x 131mm x 31mm. Interestingly, Ledger chooses not to use tamper-evident seals on its packaging, stating that they're \"easy to counterfeit and can therefore be misleading.\"\n\nInside the box, you'll find the Ledger Nano X device (obviously), in addition to a braided USB A to USB C cable and a keychain strap. Documentation includes a getting started leaflet, three recovery sheets (for recording recovery phrases) as well as several stickers featuring Ledger branding.\n\nLEDGER NANO X REVIEW: EASE OF USE\n\n [Ledger Nano X review: ease of use]The Ledger Nano X's large screen and controls make it easier to use (Image: Decrypt)\nThe Nano X may be heftier than the Nano S, but it's still a small device. As a result, navigating through the on-device menu isn't exactly the simplest process in the worldparticularly when considering the fact that it only has two buttons. However, the larger screen and controls make for a significantly less fiddly user experience than that of the Ledger Nano S.\n\nNavigating the device's menu involves scrolling left or right using the left and right button respectively, or selecting options by pressing both buttons simultaneously. Beyond this, most of the action actually occurs on the associated Ledger Live application, with the Ledger device itself being mostly used for verifying addresses and authorizing transactions.\n\nThe Ledger Nano X's larger screen resolves one of the most common gripes about the Nano S, since crypto addresses can now be displayed in their entirety instead of requiring you to scroll. One niggling issue is that the Nano X ships with a relatively short USB cablejust 50cm long, which can make it difficult to use if your computer isn't in a convenient location.\n\nLEDGER NANO X REVIEW: GETTING STARTED\n\n [Ledger Live]To get started, you'll need to use the Ledger Live app (Image: Ledger)\nTo begin using the device, you'll first need to download and install the Ledger Live client for your operating system. This is currently available for most desktop operating systems including Windows, Mac OS, Linux, as well as mobile operating systems like iOS and Android.\n\nOnce Ledger Live is up and running, you can power up the Ledger Nano X device by holding the left button, after which you'll be able to navigate through the startup screens to configure the device.\n\nThis will involve choosing a 4 to 8 digit PIN code, and backing up and verifying the randomly generated 24-word recovery phrase shown on the device. Overall, this process takes around 5 to 10 minutes, and only needs to be completed once.\n\nBy default, the device doesn't ship with any preinstalled wallet apps. Instead, these need to be manually downloaded by connecting the Ledger Nano X with Ledger Live. Thanks to its Bluetooth capabilities, the Ledger Nano X is able to pair with mobile devices running Ledger Live wirelessly; if you're using the device with a desktop PC, you'll have to use the supplied USB cable.\n\nLEDGER NANO X REVIEW: FEATURES\n\n [Ledger Nano X review: apps]The Ledger Nano X can store up to 100 apps simultaneously (Image: Decrypt)\nAs a hardware wallet, the Ledger Nano X is primarily designed for the safe storage of cryptocurrencies and other crypto assets. Because of this, the Ledger Nano X is compatible with practically every major cryptoasset, while support for new assets is added regularly.\n\nThe Ledger Nano X also overcomes one of the major limitations of its Ledger Nano S, by bumping the available internal memory from 320kb up to 2048kb. This allows users to store up to 100 apps on their device at onceconsiderably more than the 3 to 7 simultaneous apps the Ledger Nano S could hold. This means the Ledger Nano X can currently hold the entire app library simultaneouslyavoiding the need to manually remove and switch out apps due to memory constraints.\n\nWhile the vast majority of these apps allow the wallet to hold additional cryptocurrencies and tokens, a handful impart additional functionality to the Nano X. For example, the FIDO U2F app turns the device into a two-factor authentication key, whereas the recovery check app can be used to ensure you have correctly saved your recovery phrase.\n\n Ledger Nano S Review (2021): Still The Best Hardware Wallet?\n\nMoreover, the Ledger Nano X is the first cryptocurrency hardware wallet to include a built-in 100mAH battery, a necessary upgrade since the device now features Bluetooth connectivity out of the box. This allows the device to connect to mobile devices wirelessly, whereas the older Ledger Nano S could only connect to mobile devices using a Ledger OTG Kit.\n\nWith the addition of wireless connectivity, increased memory, and a much larger screen, Ledger has clearly paid attention to the shortcomings of its earlier products and is trying to make safely storing crypto assets a less challenging task.\n\nLEDGER NANO X REVIEW: SUPPORTED CRYPTO ASSETS\n\n [Ledger apps]The Ledger Nano X can store over 1,000 crypto assets (Image: Ledger)\nThe Ledger Nano X is compatible with well over 1,000 digital assets, including 23 coins and all ERC-20 tokens. Many of these can be managed through Ledger Live, whereas some require the Ledger Nano X to be used in conjunction with a compatible wallet. Supported crypto assets include;\n\n \t* Bitcoin (BTC)\n \t* Ethereum (ETH) and ERC20 tokens\n \t* XRP\n \t* Bitcoin Cash (BCH)\n \t* Litecoin (LTC)\n \t* Tether (USDT)\n \t* Binance Coin (BNB)\n \t* EOS\n \t* Stellar (XLM)\n \t* Cardano (ADA)\n \t* Monero (XMR)\n \t* Cosmos (ATOM)\n \t* Polkadot (DOT)\n \t* and over 1,000 more\n\nThe Ledger Nano X supports practically every crypto asset supported by the Ledger Nano S, but is able to hold more of the relevant wallet apps at any one time thanks to its expanded internal memory.\n\nAs such, the Ledger Nano X is ideal for securing diverse portfolios, though individuals looking to store newly released crypto assets may need to wait until Ledger adds support for them.\n\nLEDGER NANO X REVIEW: SECURITY\n\n [Ledger Nano X review: Security]The Ledger Nano X incorporates security features including a CC EAL5+ physically isolated security element (Image: Decrypt)\nAs a hardware wallet, the Ledger Nano X targets the minority of cryptocurrency users that value security above all else. As such, the team behind the product has clearly put a great deal of thought into the potential ways such a device could be attacked, and have incorporated a huge number of potential safeguards into its design.\n\nLike all Ledger devices, the Nano X features state-of-the-art security and incorporates a physically isolated security element certified as CC EAL5+. These secure elements are similar to those used to secure credit and debit cards, and are the standard used by banks for the protection of financial information.\n\nThe device also features a dual-core MCU which runs a proprietary operating system known as BOLOS and controls communication between the connected device and the Ledger secure element.\n\nAlthough the addition of Bluetooth theoretically increases the number of potential entry points hackers could use to compromise the device, the Ledger Nano X encrypts Bluetooth traffic between the mobile device and requires manual verification for all important device actions.\n\nBeyond this, Ledger's Nano X and Nano S are the only hardware wallets to receive CSPN (First Level Security Certificate) certification, which means their security has been independently certified by ANSSIthe National Cybersecurity Agency of France.\n\nThese hardware-based security measures are also supplemented with several software-based ones, including a 4-8 digital security PIN, automatic inactivity lockouts and an optional Ledger Live password lock.\n\nOverall, the Ledger Nano X is without question one of the most secure cold storage solutions on the market.\n\nHowever, although its devices offer a high level of security, Ledger has experienced some security lapses as a company.\n\nIn June 2020, data from the company's e-commerce database was leaked, resulting in over a million customer records being posted to hacker forums. Some quarter of a million records included details such as physical addresses and phone numbersexposing Ledger customers to the threat of phishing attacks and even threats.\n\n\u003eRecently,wesharednewsofadatadump.OnDecember23,wewerealertedbyoure-commerceproviderShopifyaboutanincidentinApril\u0026June'20wheretheirrogueteammembersexportedmerchants'customerdatabases.Ledgerwasincluded.Moredetails:https://t.co/NHU3IbDL0apic.twitter.com/DHQQ9arxCu\n\u003e\n\u003eLedger(@Ledger)January13,2021\n\nWhile Ledger has committed to changing how it handles customer data and identifying and prosecuting those responsible, it's an embarrassing lapse for a company whose business is the security of your crypto.\n\nLEDGER NANO X REVIEW: VERDICT\n\nThe Ledger Nano X is currently available for purchase from the official Ledger website for $119. With that said, it can often be found for cheaper at authorized third-party retailers as well as official resellers on Amazon. You should exercise caution when purchasing any hardware wallet, making sure to only purchase from authorized sources, and never using any hardware wallet that has already been configured.\n\nAt twice the price of the Ledger Nano S, the Nano X is one of the more expensive hardware wallets on the market. If portability and usability are your top concerns, it's probably worth the hit on your walletbut if you're already happy with the Ledger Nano S, there's little reason to upgrade.\n\nThe addition of Bluetooth and massively expanded internal memory are steps in the right direction, whereas the huge range of supported cryptocurrencies means that even the most diverse cryptocurrency investors can secure their entire portfolio.\n\nThe Ledger Nano X is an excellent product marred only by its high price tag; those in the market for a less expensive alternative may want to take a look at the cheaper, but dated Ledger Nano S.\n\nRATING: 4/5\n","read_this_next_post_id":"16272","read_this_next_post_type":"post","social_share_img_url":"https://cdn.decrypt.co/resize/1024/height/512/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/ledger-nano-x-review-main-gID_7.jpg","featured_image_caption":"Ledger Nano X (Image: Decrypt)","featured_image_description":"Ledger Nano X (Image: Decrypt)","featured_image_url":"https://cdn.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/01/ledger-nano-x-review-main-gID_7.jpg","primary_category":{"term_id":26172,"name":"Reviews","slug":"reviews","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":26172,"taxonomy":"category","description":"Editorial reviews and ratings for blockchain and cryptocurrency products.","parent":0,"count":0,"filter":"raw"}}},{"id":44416,"date":"2021-02-26T16:25:18","date_gmt":"2021-02-26T16:25:18","guid":{"rendered":"https://wp.decrypt.co/?p=44416"},"modified":"2021-02-26T16:29:04","modified_gmt":"2021-02-26T16:29:04","slug":"brave-web-browser-review","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https://wp.decrypt.co/44416/brave-web-browser-review/","title":{"rendered":"Brave Browser Review (2021): Earn Tokens While Browsing"},"content":{"rendered":"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eDo you remember the dark days of Internet Explorer? We do. In the face of its slow, buggy, and downright unpleasant interface, the arrival of alternative browsers like Firefox and Google Chrome was an absolute godsend. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eNow theres a (relatively) new kid on the block, and its powered by crypto: \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBrave Browser\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eWhat is Brave Browser?\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBrave Browser is a privacy-first, crypto-powered browser that blocks websites from tracking you by default.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eLaunching a new browser into the current marketplace might seem like a fools errand for Brave. Google Chrome, the market leader, has gobbled up nearly two-thirds of the \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://gs.statcounter.com/browser-market-share\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eglobal market share\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e. Apples Safari comes in a distant second, with 19%, while Mozillas Firefox brings up the rear at 4%.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBrave, however, reckons that its focus on user privacy sets it apart from the competition. Forged by the creator of JavaScript and co-founder of the Mozilla Project, Brendan Eich (who was also responsible for Firefox), Braves primary goal is to redefine how we think about browsing the web, by blocking websites from tracking you, and rewarding you with cold, hard crypto for watching ads instead.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ciframe title=\"This Is Brave\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/kLiLOkzLetE?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eThats right: Brave users can actually earn revenue in the form of \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/crypto-news/basic-attention-token\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eBasic Attention Token\u003c/a\u003e (BAT)\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e by opting to view anonymous, privacy-preserving ads. The companys ad network, which launched in November 2019, provides users with an option to watch these anonymous ads, before being paid in BAT. The service is optional, and youre more than welcome to leave all ads blocked and turned off if you wish. But were getting ahead of ourselves.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eWeve put Brave through its paces to see what its really like to use as a daily driver. Is it fast? Does it have all the features you need? Is it good enough to replace Chrome?\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eLets find out.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eDesign and UX: Familiar to Chrome users\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_44424\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-44424\" style=\"width: 1494px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-44424\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-home-screen-screenshot.jpg\" alt=\"Brave browser home screen\" width=\"1494\" height=\"840\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-home-screen-screenshot.jpg 1494w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-home-screen-screenshot-300x169.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-home-screen-screenshot-768x432.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1494px) 100vw, 1494px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-44424\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eBrave's look and feel is immediately familiar to Chrome users. Image: Brave\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eThe first time you fire up Brave on either its mobile or desktop iterations, youll be hard-pressed to spot any difference if youre coming from Chrome. Thats no coincidenceBrave is built on top of the open-source Chromium web browser that Googles own Chrome is based on.\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e\u003cbr /\u003e\n\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e\u003cbr /\u003e\n\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eFrom a UI and ease of use standpoint, that means the switch to Brave is essentially a painless one for existing Chrome users, with everything situated where youd expect it to be. Given the basic nature of web browsers in general, you wont struggle with navigation if youre coming from another browser either.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eThankfully Brave also has a built-in dark mode, which wed strongly recommend regardless of what device youre using it on. Treat your eyes to darker menus and UI layouts, and youll never want to go back to the world of piercing white screens ever again.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eGetting started with Brave browser\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBefore you dive straight into the wonderful world of cat gifs and Reddit, its worth spending a few minutes setting everything up, for a smoother, more fully-featured experience.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eThe first thing to do is import your bookmarks, which is as easy as going to Bookmarks and selecting the option toyou guessed itimport bookmarks. Choose Chrome (or any other browser you want to import information from), and, well, thats pretty much it.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=15749 data-post-title=\"Braves bonanza year, and why 2020 promises to be better still\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/15749/braves-bonanza-year-and-why-2020-promises-to-be-better-still/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eBraves bonanza year, and why 2020 promises to be better still\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eIf youre fully embracing Braves focus on privacy, you might also want to ditch Google as the default search engine and pick a less data-thirsty alternative, like DuckDuckGo, instead. Simply hit up settings, then Search engine and select your preferred service. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eThe last basic thing you might want to do is to sync up your desktop and mobile versions of Brave so that you can easily continue your sessions from one to the other, while sharing bookmarks and other preferences in the process. Go to settings, Sync and Add new device.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=43984 data-post-title=\"Privacy Browser Brave Now Available From the Dark Web\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/43984/privacy-browser-brave-dark-web-tor/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ePrivacy Browser Brave Now Available From the Dark Web\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBraves \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://brave.com/sync-v2/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003esync\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e feature can be a little clunky compared to that of Chrome, requiring you to set up a sync chain of devices by scanning a QR code or entering a 24-word keyphrase. Its nowhere near as slick as rivals offerings, which simply require you to log in; its also not yet available for iOS users.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eHow easy is Brave browser to use?\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eDespite Braves big push for privacy and blocking regular ads and trackers, there are no complicated hoops you need to jump through to benefit from these all-important core privacy features.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBrave blocks trackers and ads as standard straight out of the box, and theres something incredibly satisfying about being able to see just how much youre thwarting nefarious data mining practicesbut more on that later.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ciframe title=\"How Brave\u0026#039;s Ad Matching Works\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/aM-5SPDPtjE?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eGiven Braves Chromium DNA, you can also install whatever Chrome extension you fancy, supercharging your browsing experience any way you see fit. Thanks to the shared platform, installing extensions is as easy as visiting the Chrome web store, and clicking Add to Brave. No side-loading, no workarounds, no compatibility issues. Its as simple as that.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBrave browser speed test: faster than the competition?\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eOn both PC and mobile, we noticed no dramatic speed differences between Brave and Chrome. We wouldnt say Brave felt much or noticeably faster in any way (which is something that other users have reported), but we certainly have no complaints.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=31028 data-post-title=\"Braves massive growth signals rising concerns over privacy online\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/31028/brave-growth-users-privacy-online/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eBraves massive growth signals rising concerns over privacy online\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eTaking a more scientific method, we ran three different tests on both browsers using the tools available at \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://browserbench.org/\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" rel=\"nofollow external noopener\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003ebrowserbench.org\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e. The tests measure a mixture of JavaScript performance, graphics and the responsiveness of web applications. The results show that, in our case at least, Chrome scores slightly higher across the board in all three categories, but not by any huge margins. Raw numbers here mean very little when theres no perceptible difference in speed during normal use, so dont let that put you off.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eOne noticeable difference we did appreciate, was how much less resource-intensive Brave is compared to Chrome. Googles browser is a notorious memory hog, and throughout our benchmark tests, Chrome was using between 150-400MB more RAM than Brave. This might not seem like much, but it can make a large impact depending on the hardware youre using, so Braves lighter footprint is definitely very much appreciated.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBrave Browser: features, security, and privacy\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBrave has a number of features that make it stand out from the crowd. Its biggest selling point for most users is its Shields feature, which automatically blocks all ads and trackers. You can click the small Brave logo icon at the end of the URL bar to see how many items are blocked on the page youre on, and you can tweak the settings to make the blocking more or less aggressive, or turn it off entirely. The tool can also be used to block scripts, as well as upgrade connections to HTTPS for more security where possible.\u003c/span\u003e\u003cbr /\u003e\n\u003ciframe title=\"Privacy: Brave Browser\" width=\"640\" height=\"480\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/5z0OZABw4Eo?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eIf you want to take your private browsing one step further, you can also open the menu and select New private window with Tor. This will open up a private Tor tab, which offers far more privacy than regular incognito mode.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eRegular incognito mode prevents your browsing history, cookies, site data or information entered in forms from being stored on your device. Your browsing activity, however, can still be visible to, for example, your employer, school, or internet service provider (ISP).\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe private Tor tab purportedly offers genuine anonymity, as it hides your IP address from the sites you visit by redirecting your browsing activities through several different servers before it reaches your destination. As these connections are encrypted, your ISP or employer cant see what sites youre visitingbut there is a downside. All that re-routing has a dramatic impact on speed.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_44427\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-44427\" style=\"width: 1317px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-44427\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-tor-tab-speed-comparison.jpg\" alt=\"Brave browser speed test\" width=\"1317\" height=\"741\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-tor-tab-speed-comparison.jpg 1317w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-tor-tab-speed-comparison-300x169.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-tor-tab-speed-comparison-768x432.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1317px) 100vw, 1317px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-44427\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eBrave's Tor browser is noticeably slower. Image: speedtest.net\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eOur PC, for example, is hooked up to a router via ethernet for maximum stability and speed, and our regular download speeds measure around the 215-220 Mbps mark. In contrast, a private Tor tab measures drastically lower speeds, between 3-5 Mbps. Given that we personally dont need the extreme anonymity offered by the Tor tab in our general browsing activities, this isnt a dealbreaker by any means, and many people happily accept the tradeoff for the sake of total privacy.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eHowever, Brave's Tor integration has not been entirely bug-free. In February 2021, it was revealed that Brave had been \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/58290/brave-leaking-browsing-history-anonymous-tor-browser\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eleaking\u003c/a\u003e private .onion addresses to domain name service providers. Although the bug has since been patched, it does raise concerns over just how private Brave's private browsing features are. Indeed, in a 2019 \u003ca href=\"https://www.reddit.com/r/brave_browser/comments/a7aqxs/brave_vs_tor/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eReddit AMA\u003c/a\u003e, Brave's VP of IT Ryan Watson conceded that \"Brave with Tor does not provide the same level of Privacy as the Tor browser, if your life depends on remaining anonymous, use the Tor browser.\"\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eBrave browser wallet\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBefore we dive into how to actually earn crypto on Brave, its worth noting that it also has a built-in Ethereum crypto wallet with support for ETH and most standard Ethereum tokens and collectibles. The wallet allows you to store and send Ethereum tokens, and is similar in functionality to \u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"MetaMask review\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/50431/metamask-crypto-wallet-review\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eMetaMask\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e, except its built into the browser itself.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_44436\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-44436\" style=\"width: 1500px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-44436\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-ad-example.jpg\" alt=\"Brave browser\" width=\"1500\" height=\"799\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-ad-example.jpg 1500w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-ad-example-300x160.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-ad-example-768x409.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1500px) 100vw, 1500px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-44436\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eBrave's Binance widget lets you buy and trade crypto in-browser. Image: Brave\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eYou can also link your Binance account to a \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/27268/brave-binance-crypto-widget-launch\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003ebuilt-in widget\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e that appears on the Brave home screen, allowing you to trade, buy, and deposit crypto directly. Its a nice feature to have, but wed still prefer to use Binances own site directly. Call us old-fashioned, but trading through a widget feels a little unnerving, though well have to embrace the future eventually.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e Brave has recently announced that it's embracing the world of \u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"Our DeFi guide\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/defi-ultimate-beginners-guide-decentralized-finance\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eDeFi\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e, and will beadding a \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/59219/brave-browser-is-building-its-own-decentralized-exchange-aggregator\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003edecentralized exchange (DEX) aggregator\u003c/a\u003e to its offering, with discounts for those who hold and use BAT on the platform. But how do you get your hands on BAT? Read on\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eHow to earn crypto using Brave\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBraves most famous feature is its built-in ad system that rewards you for viewing ads with BAT tokens, while also giving you the option to contribute your earned tokens to sites that accept BAT, to support them.\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e\u003cbr /\u003e\n\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eClicking the triangular icon at the end of the URL bar shows your current BAT balance, as well as letting you know if a site has signed up to receive contributions from Brave users. If they have, then you have the option so send a tip, or set a monthly contribution.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eHit up the top right menu, select Brave Rewards, and you can tweak your experience. The settings on this screen let you turn rewards on or off, as well as tweak how many ads youre shown every hour, up to a maximum of five.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_44433\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-44433\" style=\"width: 2560px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-44433\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-wallet.jpg\" alt=\"Brave browser screenshot\" width=\"2560\" height=\"1440\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-wallet.jpg 2560w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-wallet-300x169.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-wallet-768x432.jpg 768w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-wallet-1536x864.jpg 1536w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-wallet-2048x1152.jpg 2048w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2560px) 100vw, 2560px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-44433\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eYou can earn BAT by browsing, and tip sites to show support. Image: Brave\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eIf you keep using the browser, youll eventually receive your rewards on your next payment date, which is also listed. While you can earn and contribute with BAT without signing up for anything, youll need to carry out an extra step if you want to cash it out, or contribute to your wallet from other sources.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBut if you want to cash in your BAT or contribute to your account with funds from other sources, you need to verify your wallet through Uphold, a highly rated digital currency broker. Uphold even offers a debit MasterCard that you can back with crypto.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=5751 data-post-title=\"What is Basic Attention Token (BAT)?\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/5751/basic-attention-token-bat/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eWhat is Basic Attention Token (BAT)?\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eOnce you reach a minimum of 25 BAT in your account, youll be able to verify your wallet through Uphold. Youll need to set your email and password, as well as provide your real name, birth date and phone number, as well as supply a photo of your face and ID.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eIt might sound alarming if youre not used to it, but this form of identity protection is standard practice for crypto brokers, to help verify your identity. Note that Uphold isnt currently licensed to operate in New York, though its working on getting approval.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\"price-graph\" data-date-range=1y data-id=11487\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eIts also worth noting that youre not going to be rolling in money if you turn Brave Rewards on. In 2018, Brendan Eich told \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://news.ycombinator.com/item?id=18011884\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eHacker News\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e that he would not be surprised if our users can make $70/year as we bring the system up in 2019, estimating that users would earn around $224 a year in 2020.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eIn a 2019 \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://www.reddit.com/r/BATProject/comments/ccapbp/how_much_have_you_earned_through_viewing_ads/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eReddit thread\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e, users reported earning between 20-30 BAT a month; with BATs price around $0.30, users claimed average earnings of around $6-7 BAT per month. Following the recent \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/collections/bitcoin-bull-run-2020\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ecrypto bull run\u003c/a\u003e, BAT prices have increased slightly, and currently sit at around $0.50.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBrave mobile\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_44440\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-44440\" style=\"width: 2000px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-44440\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-Mobile.jpg\" alt=\"Brave browser running on a smartphone\" width=\"2000\" height=\"1123\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-Mobile.jpg 2000w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-Mobile-300x168.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-Mobile-768x431.jpg 768w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Brave-Mobile-1536x862.jpg 1536w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 2000px) 100vw, 2000px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-44440\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eBrave is also available for Android and iOS devices. Image: Decrypt\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eIf you want to maximize your Brave rewards, or simply enjoy the same ad-free, privacy-focused experience while youre on the move, then youll be pleased to hear that you can get close to the complete Brave experience on both \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://apps.apple.com/app/brave-private-web-browser/id1052879175\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eiPhone\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e and \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.brave.browser\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eAndroid\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBraves mobile app is just as fast and slick as the desktop version, and the Shields, ad-blocking and rewards all work the same, regardless of whether you link the mobile browser to your desktop app. The only hitch we came across was the fact that the wallet and Brave rewards were both missing from our Huawei handset, although were putting that down to the lack of Googles services on Huawei handsets. Other Android devices posed no such problems.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ciframe title=\"Brave Browser iOS Speed Test\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/kHWf6hRV-GM?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003ePrivacy fiends may also want to download the Tor app separately, as the mobile version of Brave has yet to support Tor private tabs.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eBrave Today\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAs of December 2020, Brave includes the \u003ca href=\"https://brave.com/announcing-brave-today/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eBrave Today\u003c/a\u003e news feed on the start page for iOS and desktop devices (Android owners are, sadly, out of luck for the time being).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe \"privacy-preserving content stream\" uses Brave's own \u003ca href=\"https://brave.com/brave-private-cdn/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eprivate content delivery network (CDN)\u003c/a\u003e to populate its feed. It's populated locally, based on an \u003ca href=\"https://brave.com/brave-today-content/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ealgorithm\u003c/a\u003e that selects content based on how new it is, and the user's browsing historybut, crucially, no-one, even Brave, can track what you're reading.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_53206\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-53206\" style=\"width: 1920px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-53206\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/brave-today.jpg\" alt=\"Brave Today\" width=\"1920\" height=\"1005\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/brave-today.jpg 1920w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/brave-today-300x157.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/brave-today-768x402.jpg 768w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/brave-today-1536x804.jpg 1536w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1920px) 100vw, 1920px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-53206\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eBrave Today is a privacy-preserving news feed. Image: Decrypt\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn practice, it's simple to use; just scroll down from the start page to view the latest stories. Once you've viewing the news feed, a \"Customize\" button will pop up in the lower right corner of the screen; click on this to pick and choose from a selection of sources across 15 different categories, including Travel, Entertainment, Fashion and Science (you'll find \u003cem\u003eDecrypt\u003c/em\u003e listed under Crypto, gentle readers).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eDesign-wise it's a bit of a mixed bag; there's a decent selection of stories from across your chosen sources, presented in an aesthetically-pleasing layout, with tiles containing individual stories interspersed with lists from single news sources, and \"bundled\" categories. Some of the hero images are awkwardly cropped, which strips a bit of the visual polish off the layout; Brave could do with taking a leaf out of Twitter's book and using a smart \u003ca href=\"https://blog.twitter.com/engineering/en_us/topics/infrastructure/2018/Smart-Auto-Cropping-of-Images.html\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eauto-cropping algorithm\u003c/a\u003e, but it's not a deal-breaker.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eIPFS support\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn January 2021, Brave announced \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/54686/how-to-use-the-uncensorable-web-on-privacy-browser-brave\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ebuilt-in support\u003c/a\u003e for \u003ca href=\"https://ipfs.io/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eInterPlanetary File System (IPFS)\u003c/a\u003emaking it the first web browser in the world to do so. In essence, IPFS is a peer-to-peer hypermedia protocol which allows users to browse the Internet in a different way to standard HTTP.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen we use HTTP or HTTPS, our browsers use URLs to access sites that are based on centralized servers. This means that your distance to these servers affects how long it takes to load a page, and their centralized nature puts control of the information in other peoples hands. The fact that certain governments can easily block access to certain sites and information is an example of one of the main problems with the standard HTTP/S route.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ciframe title=\"How to Use IPFS With the Brave Browser\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/hpwh_zLpnCE?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIPFS, on the other hand, distributes site data across a network, in a similar vein to things like BitTorrent and blockchain, accessing content through URIs (Universal Resource Indicators) instead of URLs. In this instance, your device acts as a node that stores website data.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhen you load up an IPFS website then, youre actually loading it up from other nodes on the network. Not only does this result in faster loading times and streaming speeds, but itll also mean that websites wont go offline for everyone if a single server goes offline. Crucially, it also gives power back to the people, preventing censorship.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=57109 data-post-title=\"Decrypt Diaries: Why We Built on IPFS\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/57109/decrypt-diaries-why-we-built-on-ipfs/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eDecrypt Diaries: Why We Built on IPFS\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThere are a \u003ca href=\"https://brave.com/ipfs-support/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003efew options available\u003c/a\u003e if you want to load IPFS content through Brave. You can choose to act as a node yourself, which gives you a unique hashed ID and allows you to contribute to loading site data for other users. Alternatively, you can instead access IPFS sites via a public gateway, though these will log your IP address.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf youve got Brave 1.19 or higher, you can go to Settings \u0026gt; Extensions, and select how youd like to access IPFS content. Given that the protocol is still in its infancy compared to the long-established HTTP, there arent a huge number of IPFS sites to explorebut\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/53296/decrypt-is-now-on-ipfs-protocol-labs-filecoin\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cem\u003eDecrypt\u003c/em\u003eis one of them\u003c/a\u003e; click on the \"IPFS\" button at the bottom of any article (including this one) to view the IPFS version of the page.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIf you'd like to look farther afield,Brave has supplied its own example IPFS page, and you can find more online to test out yourselves.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWe cant actually hyperlink their example as its not recognized as a URL, which just goes to show you how early things are, so feel free to copy and paste this the old fashioned way:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eipfs://bafybeiemxf5abjwjbikoz4mc3a3dla6ual3jsgpdr4cjr3oz3evfyavhwq/wiki/Vincent_van_Gogh.html\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eVerdict\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eWell cut to the chasewere fully converted to Brave, and its now our default browser across desktop and mobile.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eIf youre a Chrome user, then the switch is a no-brainer, as youre getting the same experience in a browser that not only uses up fewer system resources, but also blocks ads, pays you to view non-tracking ads, and offers a bunch of easy to use, powerful privacy features in the process.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=17846 data-post-title=\"Why 2020 is the year of privacy\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/17846/why-2020-is-the-year-of-privacy/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eWhy 2020 is the year of privacy\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eWith so many people using Chrome already across their devices, we have no qualms recommending Brave to even technophobic family and friends.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eIn a world where it seems that everything we do is being scrutinized online, Brave is a super simple way to take some power back, while being rewarded in the processand the ability to support content creators yourself is an added bonus.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"\u003cp\u003eBraves latest update adds support for IPFS, alongside its promises of privacy protection and crypto iption":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":24493,"name":"brave ads","slug":"brave-ads","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":24493,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":4,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":9998,"name":"brave browser","slug":"brave-browser","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":9998,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":20,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":26331,"name":"brave rewards","slug":"brave-rewards","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":26331,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":3,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}}],"link":[]},"content_text":"Do you remember the dark days of Internet Explorer? We do. In the face of its slow, buggy, and downright unpleasant interface, the arrival of alternative browsers like Firefox and Google Chrome was an absolute godsend. \n\nNow theres a (relatively) new kid on the block, and its powered by crypto: Brave Browser.\n\nWHAT IS BRAVE BROWSER?\n\nBrave Browser is a privacy-first, crypto-powered browser that blocks websites from tracking you by default.\n\nLaunching a new browser into the current marketplace might seem like a fools errand for Brave. Google Chrome, the market leader, has gobbled up nearly two-thirds of the global market share. Apples Safari comes in a distant second, with 19%, while Mozillas Firefox brings up the rear at 4%.\n\nBrave, however, reckons that its focus on user privacy sets it apart from the competition. Forged by the creator of JavaScript and co-founder of the Mozilla Project, Brendan Eich (who was also responsible for Firefox), Braves primary goal is to redefine how we think about browsing the web, by blocking websites from tracking you, and rewarding you with cold, hard crypto for watching ads instead.\n\nThats right: Brave users can actually earn revenue in the form of Basic Attention Token (BAT) by opting to view anonymous, privacy-preserving ads. The companys ad network, which launched in November 2019, provides users with an option to watch these anonymous ads, before being paid in BAT. The service is optional, and youre more than welcome to leave all ads blocked and turned off if you wish. But were getting ahead of ourselves.\n\nWeve put Brave through its paces to see what its really like to use as a daily driver. Is it fast? Does it have all the features you need? Is it good enough to replace Chrome?\n\nLets find out.\n\nDESIGN AND UX: FAMILIAR TO CHROME USERS\n\n [Brave browser home screen]Brave's look and feel is immediately familiar to Chrome users. Image: Brave\nThe first time you fire up Brave on either its mobile or desktop iterations, youll be hard-pressed to spot any difference if youre coming from Chrome. Thats no coincidenceBrave is built on top of the open-source Chromium web browser that Googles own Chrome is based on.\n\nFrom a UI and ease of use standpoint, that means the switch to Brave is essentially a painless one for existing Chrome users, with everything situated where youd expect it to be. Given the basic nature of web browsers in general, you wont struggle with navigation if youre coming from another browser either.\n\nThankfully Brave also has a built-in dark mode, which wed strongly recommend regardless of what device youre using it on. Treat your eyes to darker menus and UI layouts, and youll never want to go back to the world of piercing white screens ever again.\n\nGETTING STARTED WITH BRAVE BROWSER\n\nBefore you dive straight into the wonderful world of cat gifs and Reddit, its worth spending a few minutes setting everything up, for a smoother, more fully-featured experience.\n\nThe first thing to do is import your bookmarks, which is as easy as going to Bookmarks and selecting the option toyou guessed itimport bookmarks. Choose Chrome (or any other browser you want to import information from), and, well, thats pretty much it.\n\nBraves bonanza year, and why 2020 promises to be better still\nIf youre fully embracing Braves focus on privacy, you might also want to ditch Google as the default search engine and pick a less data-thirsty alternative, like DuckDuckGo, instead. Simply hit up settings, then Search engine and select your preferred service. \n\nThe last basic thing you might want to do is to sync up your desktop and mobile versions of Brave so that you can easily continue your sessions from one to the other, while sharing bookmarks and other preferences in the process. Go to settings, Sync and Add new device.\n\n Privacy Browser Brave Now Available From the Dark Web\n\nBraves sync feature can be a little clunky compared to that of Chrome, requiring you to set up a sync chain of devices by scanning a QR code or entering a 24-word keyphrase. Its nowhere near as slick as rivals offerings, which simply require you to log in; its also not yet available for iOS users.\n\nHOW EASY IS BRAVE BROWSER TO USE?\n\nDespite Braves big push for privacy and blocking regular ads and trackers, there are no complicated hoops you need to jump through to benefit from these all-important core privacy features.\n\nBrave blocks trackers and ads as standard straight out of the box, and theres something incredibly satisfying about being able to see just how much youre thwarting nefarious data mining practicesbut more on that later.\n\nGiven Braves Chromium DNA, you can also install whatever Chrome extension you fancy, supercharging your browsing experience any way you see fit. Thanks to the shared platform, installing extensions is as easy as visiting the Chrome web store, and clicking Add to Brave. No side-loading, no workarounds, no compatibility issues. Its as simple as that.\n\nBRAVE BROWSER SPEED TEST: FASTER THAN THE COMPETITION?\n\nOn both PC and mobile, we noticed no dramatic speed differences between Brave and Chrome. We wouldnt say Brave felt much or noticeably faster in any way (which is something that other users have reported), but we certainly have no complaints.\n\n Braves massive growth signals rising concerns over privacy online\n\nTaking a more scientific method, we ran three different tests on both browsers using the tools available at browserbench.org. The tests measure a mixture of JavaScript performance, graphics and the responsiveness of web applications. The results show that, in our case at least, Chrome scores slightly higher across the board in all three categories, but not by any huge margins. Raw numbers here mean very little when theres no perceptible difference in speed during normal use, so dont let that put you off.\n\nOne noticeable difference we did appreciate, was how much less resource-intensive Brave is compared to Chrome. Googles browser is a notorious memory hog, and throughout our benchmark tests, Chrome was using between 150-400MB more RAM than Brave. This might not seem like much, but it can make a large impact depending on the hardware youre using, so Braves lighter footprint is definitely very much appreciated.\n\nBRAVE BROWSER: FEATURES, SECURITY, AND PRIVACY\n\nBrave has a number of features that make it stand out from the crowd. Its biggest selling point for most users is its Shields feature, which automatically blocks all ads and trackers. You can click the small Brave logo icon at the end of the URL bar to see how many items are blocked on the page youre on, and you can tweak the settings to make the blocking more or less aggressive, or turn it off entirely. The tool can also be used to block scripts, as well as upgrade connections to HTTPS for more security where possible.\n\nIf you want to take your private browsing one step further, you can also open the menu and select New private window with Tor. This will open up a private Tor tab, which offers far more privacy than regular incognito mode.\n\nRegular incognito mode prevents your browsing history, cookies, site data or information entered in forms from being stored on your device. Your browsing activity, however, can still be visible to, for example, your employer, school, or internet service provider (ISP).\n\nThe private Tor tab purportedly offers genuine anonymity, as it hides your IP address from the sites you visit by redirecting your browsing activities through several different servers before it reaches your destination. As these connections are encrypted, your ISP or employer cant see what sites youre visitingbut there is a downside. All that re-routing has a dramatic impact on speed.\n[Brave browser speed test]Brave's Tor browser is noticeably slower. Image: speedtest.net\nOur PC, for example, is hooked up to a router via ethernet for maximum stability and speed, and our regular download speeds measure around the 215-220 Mbps mark. In contrast, a private Tor tab measures drastically lower speeds, between 3-5 Mbps. Given that we personally dont need the extreme anonymity offered by the Tor tab in our general browsing activities, this isnt a dealbreaker by any means, and many people happily accept the tradeoff for the sake of total privacy.\n\nHowever, Brave's Tor integration has not been entirely bug-free. In February 2021, it was revealed that Brave had been leaking private .onion addresses to domain name service providers. Although the bug has since been patched, it does raise concerns over just how private Brave's private browsing features are. Indeed, in a 2019 Reddit AMA, Brave's VP of IT Ryan Watson conceded that \"Brave with Tor does not provide the same level of Privacy as the Tor browser, if your life depends on remaining anonymous, use the Tor browser.\"\n\nBRAVE BROWSER WALLET\n\nBefore we dive into how to actually earn crypto on Brave, its worth noting that it also has a built-in Ethereum crypto wallet with support for ETH and most standard Ethereum tokens and collectibles. The wallet allows you to store and send Ethereum tokens, and is similar in functionality to MetaMask, except its built into the browser itself.\n[Brave browser]Brave's Binance widget lets you buy and trade crypto in-browser. Image: Brave\nYou can also link your Binance account to a built-in widget that appears on the Brave home screen, allowing you to trade, buy, and deposit crypto directly. Its a nice feature to have, but wed still prefer to use Binances own site directly. Call us old-fashioned, but trading through a widget feels a little unnerving, though well have to embrace the future eventually.\n\n Brave has recently announced that it's embracing the world of DeFi, and will beadding a decentralized exchange (DEX) aggregator to its offering, with discounts for those who hold and use BAT on the platform. But how do you get your hands on BAT? Read on\n\nHOW TO EARN CRYPTO USING BRAVE\n\nBraves most famous feature is its built-in ad system that rewards you for viewing ads with BAT tokens, while also giving you the option to contribute your earned tokens to sites that accept BAT, to support them.\n\nClicking the triangular icon at the end of the URL bar shows your current BAT balance, as well as letting you know if a site has signed up to receive contributions from Brave users. If they have, then you have the option so send a tip, or set a monthly contribution.\n\nHit up the top right menu, select Brave Rewards, and you can tweak your experience. The settings on this screen let you turn rewards on or off, as well as tweak how many ads youre shown every hour, up to a maximum of five.\n[Brave browser screenshot]You can earn BAT by browsing, and tip sites to show support. Image: Brave\nIf you keep using the browser, youll eventually receive your rewards on your next payment date, which is also listed. While you can earn and contribute with BAT without signing up for anything, youll need to carry out an extra step if you want to cash it out, or contribute to your wallet from other sources.\n\nBut if you want to cash in your BAT or contribute to your account with funds from other sources, you need to verify your wallet through Uphold, a highly rated digital currency broker. Uphold even offers a debit MasterCard that you can back with crypto.\n\n What is Basic Attention Token (BAT)?\n\nOnce you reach a minimum of 25 BAT in your account, youll be able to verify your wallet through Uphold. Youll need to set your email and password, as well as provide your real name, birth date and phone number, as well as supply a photo of your face and ID.\n\nIt might sound alarming if youre not used to it, but this form of identity protection is standard practice for crypto brokers, to help verify your identity. Note that Uphold isnt currently licensed to operate in New York, though its working on getting approval.\n\nIts also worth noting that youre not going to be rolling in money if you turn Brave Rewards on. In 2018, Brendan Eich told Hacker News that he would not be surprised if our users can make $70/year as we bring the system up in 2019, estimating that users would earn around $224 a year in 2020.\n\nIn a 2019 Reddit thread, users reported earning between 20-30 BAT a month; with BATs price around $0.30, users claimed average earnings of around $6-7 BAT per month. Following the recent crypto bull run, BAT prices have increased slightly, and currently sit at around $0.50.\n\nBRAVE MOBILE\n\n [Brave browser running on a smartphone]Brave is also available for Android and iOS devices. Image: Decrypt\nIf you want to maximize your Brave rewards, or simply enjoy the same ad-free, privacy-focused experience while youre on the move, then youll be pleased to hear that you can get close to the complete Brave experience on both iPhone and Android.\n\nBraves mobile app is just as fast and slick as the desktop version, and the Shields, ad-blocking and rewards all work the same, regardless of whether you link the mobile browser to your desktop app. The only hitch we came across was the fact that the wallet and Brave rewards were both missing from our Huawei handset, although were putting that down to the lack of Googles services on Huawei handsets. Other Android devices posed no such problems.\n\nPrivacy fiends may also want to download the Tor app separately, as the mobile version of Brave has yet to support Tor private tabs.\n\nBRAVE TODAY\n\nAs of December 2020, Brave includes the Brave Today news feed on the start page for iOS and desktop devices (Android owners are, sadly, out of luck for the time being).\n\nThe \"privacy-preserving content stream\" uses Brave's own private content delivery network (CDN) to populate its feed. It's populated locally, based on an algorithm that selects content based on how new it is, and the user's browsing historybut, crucially, no-one, even Brave, can track what you're reading.\n[Brave Today]Brave Today is a privacy-preserving news feed. Image: Decrypt\nIn practice, it's simple to use; just scroll down from the start page to view the latest stories. Once you've viewing the news feed, a \"Customize\" button will pop up in the lower right corner of the screen; click on this to pick and choose from a selection of sources across 15 different categories, including Travel, Entertainment, Fashion and Science (you'll find _Decrypt_ listed under Crypto, gentle readers).\n\nDesign-wise it's a bit of a mixed bag; there's a decent selection of stories from across your chosen sources, presented in an aesthetically-pleasing layout, with tiles containing individual stories interspersed with lists from single news sources, and \"bundled\" categories. Some of the hero images are awkwardly cropped, which strips a bit of the visual polish off the layout; Brave could do with taking a leaf out of Twitter's book and using a smart auto-cropping algorithm, but it's not a deal-breaker.\n\nIPFS SUPPORT\n\nIn January 2021, Brave announced built-in support for InterPlanetary File System (IPFS)making it the first web browser in the world to do so. In essence, IPFS is a peer-to-peer hypermedia protocol which allows users to browse the Internet in a different way to standard HTTP.\n\nWhen we use HTTP or HTTPS, our browsers use URLs to access sites that are based on centralized servers. This means that your distance to these servers affects how long it takes to load a page, and their centralized nature puts control of the information in other peoples hands. The fact that certain governments can easily block access to certain sites and information is an example of one of the main problems with the standard HTTP/S route.\n\nIPFS, on the other hand, distributes site data across a network, in a similar vein to things like BitTorrent and blockchain, accessing content through URIs (Universal Resource Indicators) instead of URLs. In this instance, your device acts as a node that stores website data.\n\nWhen you load up an IPFS website then, youre actually loading it up from other nodes on the network. Not only does this result in faster loading times and streaming speeds, but itll also mean that websites wont go offline for everyone if a single server goes offline. Crucially, it also gives power back to the people, preventing censorship.\n\nDecrypt Diaries: Why We Built on IPFS\nThere are a few options available if you want to load IPFS content through Brave. You can choose to act as a node yourself, which gives you a unique hashed ID and allows you to contribute to loading site data for other users. Alternatively, you can instead access IPFS sites via a public gateway, though these will log your IP address.\n\nIf youve got Brave 1.19 or higher, you can go to Settings \u003e Extensions, and select how youd like to access IPFS content. Given that the protocol is still in its infancy compared to the long-established HTTP, there arent a huge number of IPFS sites to explorebut_Decrypt_is one of them; click on the \"IPFS\" button at the bottom of any article (including this one) to view the IPFS version of the page.\n\nIf you'd like to look farther afield,Brave has supplied its own example IPFS page, and you can find more online to test out yourselves.\n\nWe cant actually hyperlink their example as its not recognized as a URL, which just goes to show you how early things are, so feel free to copy and paste this the old fashioned way:\n\nipfs://bafybeiemxf5abjwjbikoz4mc3a3dla6ual3jsgpdr4cjr3oz3evfyavhwq/wiki/Vincent_van_Gogh.html\n\nVERDICT\n\nWell cut to the chasewere fully converted to Brave, and its now our default browser across desktop and mobile.\n\nIf youre a Chrome user, then the switch is a no-brainer, as youre getting the same experience in a browser that not only uses up fewer system resources, but also blocks ads, pays you to view non-tracking ads, and offers a bunch of easy to use, powerful privacy features in the process.\n\nWhy 2020 is the year of privacy\nWith so many people using Chrome already across their devices, we have no qualms recommending Brave to even technophobic family and friends.\n\nIn a world where it seems that everything we do is being scrutinized online, Brave is a super simple way to take some power back, while being rewarded in the processand the ability to support content creators yourself is an added bonus.\n","read_this_next_post_id":4013,"read_this_next_post_type":"post","social_share_img_url":"https://cdn.decrypt.co/resize/1024/height/512/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/brave-browser-review-main-gID_7.jpg","featured_image_caption":"Brave Browser is available for desktop and mobile.
