The gaming giant, which has dozens of international studios, first signaled its interest in blockchain technology by unveiling a proof-of-concept \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/4915/hashcraft-ubisoft-blockchain-future-of-gaming\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eprototype called HashCraft\u003c/a\u003e, a crypto-infused riff on Minecraft, in 2019.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ad-unit\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUbisoft has since continued on in the space by working closely with crypto gaming startups and releasing its own small-scale experiments. The publishers blockchain ambitions come from its Strategic Innovation Lab, which is headed up by Nicolas Pouard, Blockchain Initiative Director. Its a think tank and a do tank, as we like to put it, Pouard told \u003ci\u003eDecrypt\u003c/i\u003e during a recent phone interview. Our mission is to anticipate the future and help Ubisoft to be prepared for it.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=59956 data-post-title=\"Ubisoft Gets Behind a New Free-to-Play Crypto Game\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/59956/ubisoft-sorare-free-crypto-game-one-shot-league/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eUbisoft Gets Behind a New Free-to-Play Crypto Game\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUntil recently, Ubisofts moves in the space have erred more on the side of thinking than doing, primarily providing support to blockchain game developers and other crypto projects. But with the \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/59956/ubisoft-sorare-free-crypto-game-one-shot-league\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003erecent release of One Shot League\u003c/a\u003e, a free-to-play fantasy soccer game created in collaboration with Sorare, were starting to see the firm put more of those ambitions into action. Given Ubisofts stature in the game industry, it could prove to be a leading force in blockchain adoption.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eTaking their Shot\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOn one hand, One Shot League looks like an attempt to create an accessible on-ramp to Sorare and to the idea of crypto gaming as a whole. The free-to-play game, which is in the midst of its initial five-week beta season, requires a Sorare account. However, it does not force players to buy cards or handle cryptocurrencies. Tied into the last few weeks of the current Belgian Jupiler Pro League season, the game provides free digital cards for users to arrange into fantasy lineups to try and earn the most points on the in-game leaderboard.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cblockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\"\u003e\n\u003cp lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"\u003eDiscover an all-new fantasy football experience with One Shot League!\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eDeveloped by the Ubisoft Strategic Innovation Lab, build your squad for the Belgian Pro League and win digital collectible \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/SorareHQ?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e@SorareHQ\u003c/a\u003e cards  \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/NFT?src=hash\u0026amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e#NFT\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u0026mdash; Ubisoft (@Ubisoft) \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/Ubisoft/status/1366740702772789249?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eMarch 2, 2021\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cscript async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"\u003e\u003c/script\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eHowever, there are benefits to using purchased Sorare cards in the form of performance boosts. For existing Sorare players, its another way to make the most of their investment. Perhaps more importantly, for newcomers, One Shot League can be a bridge into crypto gamingwith the lure of added benefits and ongoing participation luring them into the real-deal Sorare experience.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhile officially a collaboration between Ubisoft and Sorare, the Ubisoft Strategic Lab is actually the developer behind One Shot League. It is not branded primarily as a Sorare product, but rather a separate experience that makes use of Sorares assets. According to Pouard, that was one of the big lures from their end: the prospect of interoperability between games that can seamlessly share the same crypto assets.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIts one of the big, key hooks that blockchain gaming has to offer over traditional game experiences. Crypto gaming firm Enjin, for example, has made \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/22607/enjins-multiverse-makes-ethereum-items-usable-across-games\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003einterchangeable Ethereum multiverse assets\u003c/a\u003e a key pillar of its development platform, and has even \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/30456/minecraft-gains-blockchain-assets-thanks-to-enjin-plugin\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003edeveloped a server plug-in for Minecraft\u003c/a\u003e that lets users bring cryptoassets into the game. Pouard pointed to a collaboration between \u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"Cryptokitties Beginner\u0026#039;s Guide\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/cryptokitties\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eCryptoKitties\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e and \u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"Gods Unchained review and beginner\u0026#039;s guide\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/48379/gods-unchained-review-and-beginners-guide\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eGods Unchained\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e in 2019, and said that kind of idea is something they wanted to explore further with One Shot League.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_62109\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-62109\" style=\"width: 413px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-62109 size-full\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/NICOLAS_POUARD.jpg\" alt=\"Nicolas Pouard\" width=\"413\" height=\"450\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/NICOLAS_POUARD.jpg 413w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/NICOLAS_POUARD-275x300.jpg 275w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 413px) 100vw, 413px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-62109\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eNicolas Pouard, Blockchain Innovation Director at Ubisoft. Image: Ubisoft\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSince then, we didnt really see experiments giving a real chance of building a true side game around blockchain assets built by another company. Thats what we wanted to explore: how we could change the gamers behavior using these assets, and how it could change the value of these assets, he said. How do you expand and extend the ecosystem of a game starting with the assets themselves? That was the occasion.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOne Shot League will hold another short beta season to cover the Jupiler Pro League playoffs, and then the collaborators will take the summer thereafter to evaluate the data and decide whether or not to continue on with the game. It has the potential to broaden exposure to \u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"What are NFTs?\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/non-fungible-tokens-nfts-explained-guide-learn-blockchain\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eNFTs\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e and their applications in gaming even beyond the \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/59968/nft-mania-february-trading-volume-just-topped-all-2020\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003erecent NFT boom\u003c/a\u003e, but theres no promise at this point that the game will continue on past these initial beta seasons.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"pull-quote\" data-attribution=\"Nicolas Pouard\"\u003e\"One Shot League is a way for us to help mainstream players to get a better understanding of what NFTs are.\"\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOne Shot League is a way for us to help mainstream players to get a better understanding of what NFTs are, and how you can enter this huge field of opportunity that NFTs are, said Pouard. We will see if it works or not, to be honest.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eStaying busy in the Lab\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUbisoft and Sorare have been linked for some time now through the publishers \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/10561/ubisoft-picks-eight-blockchain-startups-for-entrepreneur-lab\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eEntrepreneurs Lab accelerator program\u003c/a\u003e, which invites startups in for guidance and collaboration. The program has worked with numerous crypto startups across several seasons, including the teams behind such games as Nine Chronicles, Splinterlands, and Axie Infinity.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=35375 data-post-title=\"Gaming titan Ubisoft inks deal with blockchain RPG Nine Chronicles\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/35375/ubisoft-backs-blockchain-game-nine-chronicles/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eGaming titan Ubisoft inks deal with blockchain RPG Nine Chronicles\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSorare joined in the programs fourth season back in October 2019, and soon thereafter rose to become one of the most prominent crypto games around. The fantasy platform has more than 125 licensed teams from around the globe, including Juventus FC, Real Madrid, and \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/34080/major-league-soccer-players-ethereum-collectible-token-sorare\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eall of the Major League Soccer (MLS) squads\u003c/a\u003e, and saw its trading volume massively increase over the course of 2020. Its licensed player cards have also \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/50647/kylian-mbappe-trading-card-sells-for-65000-on-ethereum\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ebenefited from the NFT boom\u003c/a\u003e, and just before the announcement of One Shot League, Sorare announced a $50 million Series A funding round to join the \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/35842/fantasy-soccer-blockchain-game-sorare-4-million\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e$4 million seed round\u003c/a\u003e raised in July 2020.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIts never obvious that a company will meet success, but here, they had all the ingredients actually. A football or soccer card game is one of the simplest ways to aggregate all the value that an NFT can bring, said Pouard. You have the players renown, of course. You have the scarcity. And you have the fantasy itself as a football or soccer fan. You need this kind of substrate to let your imagination grow and build your own fantasy. There were a lot of good ingredients. The team is something that impressed a lot of people within Ubisoft when we worked with them in the startup program and they have a really good sense of timing.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ciframe title=\"Ubisoft Entrepreneurs Lab Season 4 : Blockchain and Extended Entertainment\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/ov9lHFI3KfA?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe Entrepreneurs Lab program allows Ubisoft exposure to an array of crypto startups that can potentially be collaborators down the line, and certainly the publishers ample resources and vast accumulated knowledge are valuable to startups looking to reach plenty of players.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eUbisofts first published crypto game, \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/32654/ubisoft-launches-rabbids-token-crypto-game-benefit-unicef\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eRabbids Token\u003c/a\u003e, came from a collaboration with another Entrepreneurs Lab alum, South African startup Wildcards. That game, launched in June 2020, riffed on the \u003ca href=\"https://www.bbc.com/news/technology-42237162\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eEthereum network-clogging CryptoKitties\u003c/a\u003e collectibles experience by letting people buy ERC-721 NFTs inspired by the popular Rayman Raving Rabbids franchise. Theres a twist, however: the owner must pay a recurring tax in ETH to hold onto the NFT, otherwise it can be snapped up by someone else without netting you any money in the process.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_62114\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-62114\" style=\"width: 1488px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-62114 size-full\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/rabbids-token.png\" alt=\"Rabbids Token screenshot\" width=\"1488\" height=\"662\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/rabbids-token.png 1488w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/rabbids-token-300x133.png 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/rabbids-token-768x342.png 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1488px) 100vw, 1488px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-62114\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eRabbids Token was Ubisoft's first published crypto game. Image: Ubisoft\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThat might seem particularly punishing, but heres the benefit: all of the money goes to charity UNICEF, plus if you did own the NFT, youll get a Proof of Plausible Ownership to add to your collection. According to the website, the project has raised 38.2 ETH (over $68,000) to date for UNICEF. Its an oddball premise for any game experience, but especially one featuring the characters and the weighty branding of Ubisoft.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWe were ending a project and we wanted to do something crazy, something different, and we really wanted to create our own NFTs and see how far we could go in the programmable aspect of things, Pouard explained. We saw in the token the opportunity to build an ever-going donation, and so first it was a side projectand really, the idea was not to build a real collectable game, but to see how far we could go in creating a new version of ERC-721.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eThe crypto gaming outlook\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAlong with publishing One Shot League and Rabbids Token, Ubisoft has also formalized its relationships with some of the aforementioned crypto game developers. The publisher is validating transactions for Axie Infinity, as well as EOS-based game store Ultra, and joined with startup accelerator Hashed on \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/35375/ubisoft-backs-blockchain-game-nine-chronicles\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ean advisory partnership for Nine Chronicles\u003c/a\u003e. Ubisoft also advises on Flow, the blockchain behind the \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60812/nba-top-shot-not-ready-surge-nft-demand\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003esurging NBA Top Shot\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAsked about some of the current crypto games that excite him personally, Pouard pointed to the play-to-earn model of Axie Infinity that has thus far produced \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/57092/biggest-ever-nft-sale-made-as-single-axie-land-goes-for-1-5-million\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eskyrocketing NFT sales\u003c/a\u003e, as well as the collectible experience of Top Shot, and the potential Roblox-esque game-as-a-platform appeal of creation game \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/42187/land-rush-crypto-whales-buy-virtual-real-estate-the-sandbox\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eThe Sandbox\u003c/a\u003e. As we are still at the beginning of this whole blockchain gaming thing, he explained, every project is trying to pave the way for their vision of what blockchain gaming could be.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003ePouard believes that the current NFT explosion could be very beneficial for helping introduce crypto gaming into the mainstream, but worries that skyrocketing item costs will impact the ability for such games to pull in users.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e[The NFT boom] helps with raising attention on blockchain gaming. My fear is that maybe all of the excitement leads to very high item values, and maybe its not a good thing for blockchain gaming, he said. Its very difficult to predict the future, but for now, we can see that it helps great teams to earn money and build their games, so thats great. It raises attention from the mainstream, so thats helpful. But we need to be very careful on the monetization side. Thats why we wanted to build a free-to-play game with One Shot League.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"pull-quote\" data-attribution=\"Nicolas Pouard\"\u003e\"[The NFT boom] helps with raising attention on blockchain gaming.\"\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhat are Ubisofts next moves in the blockchain space? Unfortunately for some whose eyes widened at the original reveal, there are no current plans to release HashCraft to the public. It is no longer in active development, but even so, its creation helped spur Ubisoft's blockchain ambitions and even influenced other creators in the space, said Pouard.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWe were very happy to see how it was inspiring for a lot of people. We discussed a lot with The Sandbox, for instance. They shared that for them, it helped them shape what The Sandbox could become, especially in the voxel part, he said. It was a proof of concept for us, a good prototype, and it was very inspiring also within Ubisoft.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_62117\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-62117\" style=\"width: 1916px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-62117 size-full\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/ubi-entrepreneurs-lab.png\" alt=\"Ubisoft Entrepreneurs Lab\" width=\"1916\" height=\"1068\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/ubi-entrepreneurs-lab.png 1916w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/ubi-entrepreneurs-lab-300x167.png 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/ubi-entrepreneurs-lab-768x428.png 768w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/ubi-entrepreneurs-lab-1536x856.png 1536w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1916px) 100vw, 1916px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-62117\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eUbisoft's Entrepreneurs Lab. Image: Ubisoft\u003c/figcaption\u003e\u003c/figure\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBut the Ubisoft stable has a lot of distinctive and very popular properties within it, like the aforementioned Just Dance and Assassin's Creed. Much like Rabbids Token turned a classic franchise into something new and compelling with a crypto twist, Pouard acknowledges that theyre looking at other potential franchise extensions.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eYeah, of course. Thats our work at the Strategic Innovation Lab, to explore the future of the blockchain field and NFTs, so of course we are continuing to explore the field, he said when asked about potential crypto gaming projects based on existing Ubisoft franchises. I can say Yeah. Its not a promise, but its our work to explore and to see the new kind of opportunities and the way it will change the industry.\u003c/p\u003e\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"\u003cp\u003eGaming giant Ubisoft continues to explore the possibilities of blockchain gaming, from NFTs you can share between gaming","slug":"blockchain-gaming","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":4006,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":24,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":31071,"name":"crypto gaming","slug":"crypto-gaming","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":31071,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":6,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":30035,"name":"game industry","slug":"game-industry","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":30035,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":2,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":5854,"name":"Ubisoft","slug":"ubisoft","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":5854,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":20,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}}],"link":[]},"content_text":"The blockchain gaming world is largely populated by startups built specifically to pioneer the burgeoning industry of crypto games, whether its Immutable with card-battler Gods Unchained, Sorare with its popular fantasy soccer platform, or Sky Mavis behind the Pokmon-inspired Axie Infinity.\n\nHowever, there is one very big exception: Ubisoft, one of the largest traditional game publishers in the world, and the storied brand behind mega-franchises like Assassins Creed, Far Cry, Just Dance, and various Tom Clancy-branded shooters. The gaming giant, which has dozens of international studios, first signaled its interest in blockchain technology by unveiling a proof-of-concept prototype called HashCraft, a crypto-infused riff on Minecraft, in 2019.\n\nUbisoft has since continued on in the space by working closely with crypto gaming startups and releasing its own small-scale experiments. The publishers blockchain ambitions come from its Strategic Innovation Lab, which is headed up by Nicolas Pouard, Blockchain Initiative Director. Its a think tank and a do tank, as we like to put it, Pouard told _Decrypt_ during a recent phone interview. Our mission is to anticipate the future and help Ubisoft to be prepared for it.\n\nUbisoft Gets Behind a New Free-to-Play Crypto Game\nUntil recently, Ubisofts moves in the space have erred more on the side of thinking than doing, primarily providing support to blockchain game developers and other crypto projects. But with the recent release of One Shot League, a free-to-play fantasy soccer game created in collaboration with Sorare, were starting to see the firm put more of those ambitions into action. Given Ubisofts stature in the game industry, it could prove to be a leading force in blockchain adoption.\n\nTAKING THEIR SHOT\n\nOn one hand, One Shot League looks like an attempt to create an accessible on-ramp to Sorare and to the idea of crypto gaming as a whole. The free-to-play game, which is in the midst of its initial five-week beta season, requires a Sorare account. However, it does not force players to buy cards or handle cryptocurrencies. Tied into the last few weeks of the current Belgian Jupiler Pro League season, the game provides free digital cards for users to arrange into fantasy lineups to try and earn the most points on the in-game leaderboard.\n\n\u003eDiscoveranall-newfantasyfootballexperiencewithOneShotLeague!\n\u003e\n\u003eDevelopedbytheUbisoftStrategicInnovationLab,buildyoursquadfortheBelgianProLeagueandwindigitalcollectible@SorareHQcards#NFT\n\u003e\n\u003eUbisoft(@Ubisoft)March2,2021\n\nHowever, there are benefits to using purchased Sorare cards in the form of performance boosts. For existing Sorare players, its another way to make the most of their investment. Perhaps more importantly, for newcomers, One Shot League can be a bridge into crypto gamingwith the lure of added benefits and ongoing participation luring them into the real-deal Sorare experience.\n\nWhile officially a collaboration between Ubisoft and Sorare, the Ubisoft Strategic Lab is actually the developer behind One Shot League. It is not branded primarily as a Sorare product, but rather a separate experience that makes use of Sorares assets. According to Pouard, that was one of the big lures from their end: the prospect of interoperability between games that can seamlessly share the same crypto assets.\n\nIts one of the big, key hooks that blockchain gaming has to offer over traditional game experiences. Crypto gaming firm Enjin, for example, has made interchangeable Ethereum multiverse assets a key pillar of its development platform, and has even developed a server plug-in for Minecraft that lets users bring cryptoassets into the game. Pouard pointed to a collaboration between CryptoKitties and Gods Unchained in 2019, and said that kind of idea is something they wanted to explore further with One Shot League.\n[Nicolas Pouard]Nicolas Pouard, Blockchain Innovation Director at Ubisoft. Image: Ubisoft\nSince then, we didnt really see experiments giving a real chance of building a true side game around blockchain assets built by another company. Thats what we wanted to explore: how we could change the gamers behavior using these assets, and how it could change the value of these assets, he said. How do you expand and extend the ecosystem of a game starting with the assets themselves? That was the occasion.\n\nOne Shot League will hold another short beta season to cover the Jupiler Pro League playoffs, and then the collaborators will take the summer thereafter to evaluate the data and decide whether or not to continue on with the game. It has the potential to broaden exposure to NFTs and their applications in gaming even beyond the recent NFT boom, but theres no promise at this point that the game will continue on past these initial beta seasons.\n\n\"One Shot League is a way for us to help mainstream players to get a better understanding of what NFTs are.\"\nOne Shot League is a way for us to help mainstream players to get a better understanding of what NFTs are, and how you can enter this huge field of opportunity that NFTs are, said Pouard. We will see if it works or not, to be honest.\n\nSTAYING BUSY IN THE LAB\n\nUbisoft and Sorare have been linked for some time now through the publishers Entrepreneurs Lab accelerator program, which invites startups in for guidance and collaboration. The program has worked with numerous crypto startups across several seasons, including the teams behind such games as Nine Chronicles, Splinterlands, and Axie Infinity.\n\nGaming titan Ubisoft inks deal with blockchain RPG Nine Chronicles\nSorare joined in the programs fourth season back in October 2019, and soon thereafter rose to become one of the most prominent crypto games around. The fantasy platform has more than 125 licensed teams from around the globe, including Juventus FC, Real Madrid, and all of the Major League Soccer (MLS) squads, and saw its trading volume massively increase over the course of 2020. Its licensed player cards have also benefited from the NFT boom, and just before the announcement of One Shot League, Sorare announced a $50 million Series A funding round to join the $4 million seed round raised in July 2020.\n\nIts never obvious that a company will meet success, but here, they had all the ingredients actually. A football or soccer card game is one of the simplest ways to aggregate all the value that an NFT can bring, said Pouard. You have the players renown, of course. You have the scarcity. And you have the fantasy itself as a football or soccer fan. You need this kind of substrate to let your imagination grow and build your own fantasy. There were a lot of good ingredients. The team is something that impressed a lot of people within Ubisoft when we worked with them in the startup program and they have a really good sense of timing.\n\nThe Entrepreneurs Lab program allows Ubisoft exposure to an array of crypto startups that can potentially be collaborators down the line, and certainly the publishers ample resources and vast accumulated knowledge are valuable to startups looking to reach plenty of players.\n\nUbisofts first published crypto game, Rabbids Token, came from a collaboration with another Entrepreneurs Lab alum, South African startup Wildcards. That game, launched in June 2020, riffed on the Ethereum network-clogging CryptoKitties collectibles experience by letting people buy ERC-721 NFTs inspired by the popular Rayman Raving Rabbids franchise. Theres a twist, however: the owner must pay a recurring tax in ETH to hold onto the NFT, otherwise it can be snapped up by someone else without netting you any money in the process.\n[Rabbids Token screenshot]Rabbids Token was Ubisoft's first published crypto game. Image: Ubisoft\nThat might seem particularly punishing, but heres the benefit: all of the money goes to charity UNICEF, plus if you did own the NFT, youll get a Proof of Plausible Ownership to add to your collection. According to the website, the project has raised 38.2 ETH (over $68,000) to date for UNICEF. Its an oddball premise for any game experience, but especially one featuring the characters and the weighty branding of Ubisoft.\n\nWe were ending a project and we wanted to do something crazy, something different, and we really wanted to create our own NFTs and see how far we could go in the programmable aspect of things, Pouard explained. We saw in the token the opportunity to build an ever-going donation, and so first it was a side projectand really, the idea was not to build a real collectable game, but to see how far we could go in creating a new version of ERC-721.\n\nTHE CRYPTO GAMING OUTLOOK\n\nAlong with publishing One Shot League and Rabbids Token, Ubisoft has also formalized its relationships with some of the aforementioned crypto game developers. The publisher is validating transactions for Axie Infinity, as well as EOS-based game store Ultra, and joined with startup accelerator Hashed on an advisory partnership for Nine Chronicles. Ubisoft also advises on Flow, the blockchain behind the surging NBA Top Shot.\n\nAsked about some of the current crypto games that excite him personally, Pouard pointed to the play-to-earn model of Axie Infinity that has thus far produced skyrocketing NFT sales, as well as the collectible experience of Top Shot, and the potential Roblox-esque game-as-a-platform appeal of creation game The Sandbox. As we are still at the beginning of this whole blockchain gaming thing, he explained, every project is trying to pave the way for their vision of what blockchain gaming could be.\n\nPouard believes that the current NFT explosion could be very beneficial for helping introduce crypto gaming into the mainstream, but worries that skyrocketing item costs will impact the ability for such games to pull in users.\n\n[The NFT boom] helps with raising attention on blockchain gaming. My fear is that maybe all of the excitement leads to very high item values, and maybe its not a good thing for blockchain gaming, he said. Its very difficult to predict the future, but for now, we can see that it helps great teams to earn money and build their games, so thats great. It raises attention from the mainstream, so thats helpful. But we need to be very careful on the monetization side. Thats why we wanted to build a free-to-play game with One Shot League.\n\n\"[The NFT boom] helps with raising attention on blockchain gaming.\"\nWhat are Ubisofts next moves in the blockchain space? Unfortunately for some whose eyes widened at the original reveal, there are no current plans to release HashCraft to the public. It is no longer in active development, but even so, its creation helped spur Ubisoft's blockchain ambitions and even influenced other creators in the space, said Pouard.\n\nWe were very happy to see how it was inspiring for a lot of people. We discussed a lot with The Sandbox, for instance. They shared that for them, it helped them shape what The Sandbox could become, especially in the voxel part, he said. It was a proof of concept for us, a good prototype, and it was very inspiring also within Ubisoft.\n[Ubisoft Entrepreneurs Lab]Ubisoft's Entrepreneurs Lab. Image: Ubisoft\nBut the Ubisoft stable has a lot of distinctive and very popular properties within it, like the aforementioned Just Dance and Assassin's Creed. Much like Rabbids Token turned a classic franchise into something new and compelling with a crypto twist, Pouard acknowledges that theyre looking at other potential franchise extensions.\n\nYeah, of course. Thats our work at the Strategic Innovation Lab, to explore the future of the blockchain field and NFTs, so of course we are continuing to explore the field, he said when asked about potential crypto gaming projects based on existing Ubisoft franchises. I can say Yeah. Its not a promise, but its our work to explore and to see the new kind of opportunities and the way it will change the industry.\n","read_this_next_post_id":61460,"read_this_next_post_type":"post","social_share_img_url":"https://cdn.decrypt.co/resize/1024/height/512/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/hashcraft-gID_1.jpg","featured_image_caption":"Ubisoft's blockchain-powered game Hashcraft. Ethereums ongoing upgrade, \u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"What is Ethereum 2.0\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/what-is-ethereum-2-0\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eEthereum 2.0\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e, is designed to mitigate those concerns.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eIn the meantime, Ethereum cofounder Vitalik Buterin has proposed \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60878/vitalik-buterin-touts-100x-scaling-solution-for-ethereum\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003einterim scaling measures\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e. Some community improvement proposals have not gone down well with miners, who fear a reduction in their fees of as much as 50%. A new proposal, EIP-3368, would see block rewards reduced by 0.25 ETH every quarter, helping to ease the impact of Ethereums transition to proof-of-stake on miners.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=57827 data-post-title=\"Coinbase Opens Waitlist for Ethereum 2.0 Staking Rewards\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/57827/coinbase-opens-waitlist-for-ethereum-2-0-staking-rewards/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eCoinbase Opens Waitlist for Ethereum 2.0 Staking Rewards\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eJPR noted that upcoming changes to the Ethereum ecosystem mean that demand for GPUs among crypto miners is likely to evaporate, as the blockchain network transitions to Eth 2.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eHowever, this will take some time. The network will be upgraded in phases, and the last isnt scheduled to happen until 2022assuming there are no delays.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cfigure id=\"attachment_42330\" aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-42330\" style=\"width: 1600px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"\u003e\u003cimg loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-42330\" src=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/shutterstock_1606529806.jpg\" alt=\"NVIDIA logo\" width=\"1600\" height=\"900\" srcset=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/shutterstock_1606529806.jpg 1600w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/shutterstock_1606529806-300x169.jpg 300w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/shutterstock_1606529806-768x432.jpg 768w, https://wp.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/shutterstock_1606529806-1536x864.jpg 1536w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1600px) 100vw, 1600px\" /\u003e\u003cfigcaption id=\"caption-attachment-42330\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"\u003eNVIDIA is one of the world's leading graphic chip producers. mining","slug":"cryptocurrency-mining","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":12214,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":12,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":195,"name":"Ethereum","slug":"ethereum","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":195,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":1548,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":3867,"name":"gpu","slug":"gpu","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":3867,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":7,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":29411,"name":"nvidia","slug":"nvidia","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":29411,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":16,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}}],"link":[]},"content_text":"Ever since cryptocurrency miners realized that the graphics processing units (GPUs) used to process the demanding visuals for modern PC games could be turned to the task of crunching numbers to produce crypto, gamers and miners have been at loggerheads. Miners have snapped up stocks of GPUs as soon as they come on the market, sending prices soaring and leaving gamers empty-handed.\n\nThose tensions threatened to burst forth last week, as reports spread that so-called hash-rate limitsapplied by GPU manufacturer Nvidia to reduce a chips efficiency when mining cryptocurrencies such as Ethereumhad been compromised.\n\nThe news was subsequently debunked, and experts said it was almost impossible to get around the restrictions, which slash RTX 3060 crypto mining capacity by 50%. Subsequently, multiple reports have claimed that a beta driver release bypasses Nvidias restrictions.\n\nThe furor highlights growing apprehension in the chip industry, as principal manufacturers Nvidia and AMD seek to accommodate the needs of both gamers and crypto miners. It comes amid a surge in crypto mining revenues that's seen mining operators desperate to buy up inventoryleading to skyrocketing prices for GPUs.\n\nChip manufacturers, meanwhile, are hampered by the scarcity of raw materials needed and confounded by Ethereums shift to a proof-of-stake consensus model, which will ultimately do away with mining altogether.\n\nETHEREUM-DEDICATED GPUS\n\nIn February this year, Nvidia launched a dedicated chipset aimed at crypto miners, targeting Ethereum. At the same time, it throttled the hash rate of its new RTX 3060 GPUs in an effort to make them less desirable to crypto miners.\n\nThe chipmakers moves came in response to gamers who were concerned about GPU shortages due to demand from miners. Ethereum was specifically targeted because it had the highest mining yield among GPU-mineable coins, according to Nvidia.\n\n\u003eDammitChinesemodpic.twitter.com/dBNjpJQLMl\n\u003e\n\u003eI_Leak_VN(@I_Leak_VN)March10,2021\n\nBut chip shortages have meant that crypto miners have even resorted to gaming laptops to wring out extra hash rate and benefit from bull-run profits. So, for some, it wasnt so surprising when screenshots, posted by the Twitter account @I_Leak_VN, suggested that enterprising Chinese Ethereum miners had found a way to bypass the restrictions.\n\nLater it transpired that the screenshots werent of Ethereum, but another blockchain altogether. Mining experts said that only an Nvidia insider would be able to make the changes needed. However, since then experts from industry publications _PC Watch_, _Computer Base_, and _Hardwareluxx _have debunked _their _claims, revealing that a recent Nvidia beta driver release bypasses the manufacturer's hash rate limits_._\n\n\u003eNvidiasnewbetadriverunlocksRTX3060Ethereumcryptocurrencymininghttps://t.co/XYRJzXUJxQpic.twitter.com/zj1LZZKwJT\n\u003e\n\u003eTheVerge(@verge)March15,2021\n\nMeanwhile, Nvidias rival AMD is reportedly developing its own dedicated mining chipset too; the latest version of the AMD Navi 12, initially used for the Apple Macbook Pro. It has no video outputs (which are mandatory for gaming) according to _PC Gamer_. That means the GPU could be the first crypto mining-related specific processor launched by the company, and it specifically targets Ethereum miners.\n\nThese recent moves by both AMD and Nvidia signal attempts to segregate GPUs used for crypto mining, from those used for gaming. But not everyone believes thats the strategy the multinational should be following.\n\nETHEREUM MINING REVENUES SOAR\n\nEarlier this month, Nvidia won a landmark lawsuit, which dismissed investors claims that the chip manufacturer hid its reliance on its burgeoning cryptocurrency mining business to the tune of more than $1 billion. The action was initiated two years ago by investors concerned that Nvidias profits were becoming too closely entwined with the volatile cryptocurrency market. But their claims were dismissed due to a lack of evidence that the company misled anyone.\n\nNvidia Wins Lawsuit Over Alleged $1 Billion Crypto Mining Biz\nNow, the situation is somewhat different. A surge in the popularity of crypto mining followed PayPals decision to integrate cryptocurrencies and high-profile investor interest. This contributed to a significant surge in GPU sales in Q4 2020, with GPU shipments rising by 20.5% quarter-on-quarter and by 12.4% over Q4 2019, according to a report published this month.\n\nAnalysts, Jon Peddie Research (JPR), who are behind the report, claimed that mining, specifically on the Ethereum network, played a sizeable role.\n\nThis year, Ethereum network fees earned by miners more than doubled, even from last years peak during the craze for decentralized finance (DeFi) last summer, and miners saw their revenue triple. No other cryptocurrency comes close to Ethereum for mining profitability right now, according to mining experts.\n\n\u003eThefeesaretoodamnhigh!\n\u003e\n\u003eEthereumminerrevenuehastripledprevioushighsreachedduringthissummer'sDeFiboompic.twitter.com/isom1cYavk\n\u003e\n\u003eMessari(@MessariCrypto)March4,2021\n\nThe flip side of this success was that an average transaction fee reached $38.21 on Feb 23, making the network unviable for smaller transactions (and impacting on activity in the burgeoning DeFi space). Ethereums ongoing upgrade, Ethereum 2.0, is designed to mitigate those concerns.\n\nIn the meantime, Ethereum cofounder Vitalik Buterin has proposed interim scaling measures. Some community improvement proposals have not gone down well with miners, who fear a reduction in their fees of as much as 50%. A new proposal, EIP-3368, would see block rewards reduced by 0.25 ETH every quarter, helping to ease the impact of Ethereums transition to proof-of-stake on miners.\n\nCoinbase Opens Waitlist for Ethereum 2.0 Staking Rewards\nJPR noted that upcoming changes to the Ethereum ecosystem mean that demand for GPUs among crypto miners is likely to evaporate, as the blockchain network transitions to Eth 2.\n\nHowever, this will take some time. The network will be upgraded in phases, and the last isnt scheduled to happen until 2022assuming there are no delays.\n[NVIDIA logo]NVIDIA is one of the world's leading graphic chip producers. Image: Shutterstock\nBy that time, another proof-of-work cryptocurrency could become profitable enough to take Ethereums place, but most so-called third-generation blockchains, such as Cardano and Polkadot, have launched with proof of stakemaking that rather unlikely.\n\nAnd switching to Bitcoin, Bitcoin Cash, Litecoinor other high-profile proof-of-work cryptocurrencies is impossible for miners, because they utilize a different hashing algorithm.\n\nSo, perhaps gamers have little cause to worrylong-term at least. In the meantime, any old graphics cards they have lying around could well be worth a tidy sum to an Ethereum miner. \n","read_this_next_post_id":"60878","read_this_next_post_type":"post","social_share_img_url":"https://cdn.decrypt.co/resize/1024/height/512/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/geforce-rtx-3060-ti-1-gID_5.jpeg","featured_image_caption":"Nvidia's RTX 3060 Ti. Image: Nvidia.","featured_image_description":"Nvidia's RTX 3060 Ti. Image: Nvidia.","featured_image_url":"https://cdn.decrypt.co/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/geforce-rtx-3060-ti-1-gID_5.jpeg","primary_category":{"term_id":23621,"name":"Features","slug":"features","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":23621,"taxonomy":"category","description":"Deep dives into Web 3.0, future and present.","parent":0,"count":1,"filter":"raw"}}},{"id":60394,"date":"2021-03-13T12:03:54","date_gmt":"2021-03-13T12:03:54","guid":{"rendered":"https://wp.decrypt.co/?p=60394"},"modified":"2021-03-13T14:03:03","modified_gmt":"2021-03-13T14:03:03","slug":"nft-craze-easy-money-hard-copyright-questions","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https://wp.decrypt.co/60394/nft-craze-easy-money-hard-copyright-questions/","title":{"rendered":"The NFT Craze Offers Easy MoneyAnd Hard Copyright Questions"},"content":{"rendered":"\u003cp\u003eIf there was a contest for acronym of the year, \"NFT\" would be the clear favorite for 2021. Short for non-fungible tokens, \u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"What are NFTs?\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/non-fungible-tokens-nfts-explained-guide-learn-blockchain\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eNFTs\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e are having a moment as fans scramble to \"own\" pieces of digital art or pop culture moments.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhile many people are baffled by the trend, no one can deny it's been lucrative. In recent weeks, buyers have laid down millions of dollars to acquire NFTs issued by the likes of the artist \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/50922/beeple-ethereum-nft-art-sale\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eBeeple\u003c/a\u003e and the musician \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/59827/grimes-nfts-crypto-art\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eGrimes\u003c/a\u003e.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBut along with the money and hype, the NFT craze has spurred a debate over what it means to own digital property, and the role of copyright on the Internet. Some suggest NFTs might soothe long-running tensions between creators and tech platformswhile others point out the trend has already given rise to new forms of piracy and rip-offs.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eWhat exactly are people buying?\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eNFTs are not new. They've been around since 2017 when a company called Dapper Labs began selling NFTs in the form of unique digital cat cartoons called \u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"Cryptokitties Beginner\u0026#039;s Guide\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/cryptokitties\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eCryptoKitties\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e. Those kitties were the subject of a short-lived craze, and some sold for tens of thousands of dollars before the fad quickly fizzled. Now, in 2021, NFTs have come roaring back as the phenomenon has expanded well beyond digital cats.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ad-unit\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eToday, the range of NFTs for sale includes just about anything that can be captured as a digital file. The band Kings of Leon, for instance, \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60087/kings-of-leon-nft\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003edropped NFT versions of their new album\u003c/a\u003e, while the NBA is selling \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60391/nba-built-for-top-shot-nft-craze\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eNFT basketball highlights\u003c/a\u003e. An original work by street artist Banksy has been burned and \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60070/an-original-banksy-has-been-burned-and-turned-into-an-nft\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eturned into an NFT\u003c/a\u003e. And last week, the bidding for an NFT of Twitter founder Jack Dorsey's \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60415/jack-dorsey-selling-first-tweet-nft\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003efirst tweet\u003c/a\u003e topped $2 million.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAll of this raises the question of \u003cem\u003ejust what are people buying\u003c/em\u003e? After all, any of these NFT artifacts can be easily copiedlegally or otherwiseby anyone with an Internet connection and a basic familiarity with software. Why pay to \"own\" Jack Dorsey's tweet when you can print out or embed the same tweet on a website like I've done below?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cblockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\"\u003e\n\u003cp lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"\u003ejust setting up my twttr\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u0026mdash; jack (@jack) \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/jack/status/20?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eMarch 21, 2006\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cscript async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"\u003e\u003c/script\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eNFT enthusiasts will tell you that the artifact they bought might look (or sound) identical to copies on the Internet, but \u003cem\u003etheir\u003c/em\u003e version comes with a unique ownership certificate. That certificate is inscribed on a blockchain to create a tamper-proof transaction record to show the world that the artworkor song or sports highlightbelongs to someone. Think of it as a serial number or a signature from the artist.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhat this means, at least to NFT boosters, is that they own something unique. Just as an original painting signed by a famous artist is worth millions, even though thousands of college students tape the same image to their dorm room, NFT owners claim that their piece of digital art is the \"real\" one.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eNonetheless, NFT owners might be surprised to discover that what they \"own\" is rather limited.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAs law professors like to tell their students, property is like a bundle of sticks. Each stick in the bundle represents a right to do something, such as the right to sell the piece of property, or harvest it or destroy it, and so on. This is certainly true of copyright, which contains more sticks in its bundlesuch as the right to broadcast and merchandise an imagethan many people realize.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn the case of sports leagues and musical acts, lawyers are taking pains to ensure their clients keep most of the ownership sticks in the copyright bundle for themselves. For fans, what they receive when buying an NFT is a license that lets them do little beyond display or transfer the work. Purchasers of \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60808/so-you-bought-an-nba-top-shot-nft-what-do-you-actually-own\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eNFTs issued by the NBA\u003c/a\u003ecalled \"Moments\"can't, for instance, modify the highlight they buy, or display it in a way the league considers hateful or offensive.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=60808 data-post-title=\"So You Bought an NBA Top Shot NFT. What Do You Actually Own?\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/60808/so-you-bought-an-nba-top-shot-nft-what-do-you-actually-own/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eSo You Bought an NBA Top Shot NFT. What Do You Actually Own?\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSome of these limits go beyond those that go with owning a physical pack of sports cards. In the case of those physical cardswhich the NBA likes to invoke as a comparison to NFTsthe owner is free to draw mustaches on the players, or glue the card to a controversial collage. This might not be the case with NFTs. One can imagine a situation in which pro-democracy activists use their NFTs to call attention to the NBA's attempts to cozy up to China, and the league responds by deleting the NFTs.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThere are limits to what you can do with a physical card too, of course. Sports leagues' intellectual property rights mean you can't replicate the card images for a t-shirt business, but the rights are certainly broader than what attaches to these NFTs.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eA new form of property brings new forms of piracy\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTonya Evans, an intellectual property scholar at Penn State Dickinson Law, studies blockchains and NFTs and wrote an influential 2018 paper on the CryptoKitties phenomenon. She believes that NFTs offer an important new way for creators to connect and earn money from their fans.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eShe notes that a number of Black artists have been at the forefront of the NFT craze, using forums like the new social media audio app Clubhouse to market and sell their works. Evans says that the tech underlying NFT provides a way to counteract the Internet's capacity for endless replication and lets artists prove a digital work is unique.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\"You can code for the integrity of the work,\" said Evans. \"Technology threatened the music industry, letting anyone make a perfect digital copy of the original, and now maybe this is the technology that can cure that.\"\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eEvans is right that NFT tech offers new opportunities for creators. It's not just prominent artists like Grimes or Beeple that are making real money selling NFTs. So are lesser-known artists, who are using platforms like Nifty Gateway and OpenSea to sell limited edition prints of sneakers and boomboxes. In this sense, NFTs represent a new spigot of money that didn't exist before.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=61241 data-post-title=\"Can NFTs Change How We Value Music?\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/61241/can-nfts-change-how-we-value-music/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eCan NFTs Change How We Value Music?\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eBut like everything else on the Internet that makes money, the NFT craze has attracted parasitic bad actors looking to cash in on the works of others. That's what happened to an artist who creates digital pictures under the name Weird Undead. She discovered someone has been stealing her images and selling them as NFTs:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cblockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\"\u003e\n\u003cp lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"\u003eI tried to ignore whole \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/NFT?src=hash\u0026amp;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e#NFT\u003c/a\u003e hysteria but WHAT THE FUCK\u003cbr /\u003eI don\u0026#39;t give any permission (ESPECIALLY to random jerks) to make tokens from my content and I feel so angry \u003ca href=\"https://t.co/E9UKF1AXug\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003epic.twitter.com/E9UKF1AXug\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u0026mdash; don\u0026#39;t give up, skeleton (@WeirdUndead) \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/WeirdUndead/status/1369210982518693888?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eMarch 9, 2021\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cscript async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"\u003e\u003c/script\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn the last week, Weird Undead (who asked \u003cem\u003eDecrypt\u003c/em\u003e not to use her real name) has been filing a flurry of legal notices with OpenSeaone of the biggest NFT marketswhile her fans have been doing the same so as to stop what she calls \"insane and pointless copyright infringement.\" She has also discovered that copycats have been using a service called Tokenized Tweets to create and sell tweets based on her work, and asked it to stop.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eMeanwhile, influential figures in the cryptocurrency industry, including Meltem Demirors of CoinShares and Neeraj Agrawal of Coin Center, have complained of random people repackaging their tweets as tokens for sale:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cblockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\"\u003e\n\u003cp lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"\u003eits pretty annoying\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u0026mdash; Neeraj K. Agrawal (@NeerajKA) \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/NeerajKA/status/1369365838881566728?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eMarch 9, 2021\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cscript async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"\u003e\u003c/script\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eHucksters flogging unauthorized tokens are just one part of the emerging piracy problems surrounding NFTs. A potentially more serious one is the emergence of competing blockchain services, each of which promise that \u003cem\u003ethey\u003c/em\u003e provide the authoritative record that a given NFT is unique. The situation is akin to a town having two competing services to register land deeds, or two auction houses each claiming they have the legitimate title to a piece of fine art. The issue is potentially an existential one for the nascent NFT industry, which stakes its existence on being able to prove a given token is unique.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSo far, the main NFT marketplaces are cooperating, with each agreeing to recognize a token as unique even when it passes from one forum to another. But that hasn't stopped the users of Binances blockchain from hosting rogue token shops on the network, which not only sold plagiarized works but also clearly \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60125/binance-smart-chains-musical-beats-alleged-ethereum-copycat-shuts-down-days-after-launch\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003emimicked the store names\u003c/a\u003e of existing Ethereum-based NFT shopsfor instance \"Binance Punks\" for \"Crypto Punks\" and \"Bashmasks\" for \"Hashmasks.\"\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=60125 data-post-title=\"Binance Smart Chain's Musical Beats, Alleged Ethereum Copycat, Shuts Down Days After Launch\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/60125/binance-smart-chains-musical-beats-alleged-ethereum-copycat-shuts-down-days-after-launch/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eBinance Smart Chain's Musical Beats, Alleged Ethereum Copycat, Shuts Down Days After Launch\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhile trademark and copyright law provides a remedy for rip-offs, it's likely to prove difficult for artists to find and sue an infringer, since blockchains, by their nature, are designed to be borderless and decentralized. This would explain why some upset by recent behavior on Binance's network resorted to non-legal measures to express their displeasureincluding \u003ca href=\"https://www.yahoo.com/now/controversial-dapps-test-binance-smart-233029970.html\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eposting\u003c/a\u003e images from the Tiananmen Square massacre on the company's blockchain. (Binance has ties to China).\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSuch disputes raise the question of whether NFTs represent just the latest headache for creators trying to make a living from their work. But while NFTs can pose a nuisance, some are optimistic these problems are outweighed by the potential for artists to earn a new form of incomeand that NFTs could reshape how we view copyright and the Internet.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003eA breakthrough in the copyright debate?\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eEven since consumers began using it en masse in the mid-1990s, the Internet has proved a mixed blessing for artists, writers, and other creators. On one hand, the web provides an enormous new platform to reach fans and find new audiences. On the other, it's awash with pirates who copy an artist's work and sell it or give it away for nothing. Meanwhile, the giant tech platforms like Amazon and Spotify have come to enjoy virtual monopolies when it comes to selling digital works and, in the view of critics, failed to pay out a fair share to artists.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAll of this has led to two decades of debate about copyright policy. The debate is often bitter with the entertainment industry accusing tech enthusiasts of supporting piracy and robbing artistswhile opponents accuse the industry of lobbying Congress to pass copyright laws that they view as draconian and prone to abuse.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe rise of NFTs could help transcend this debate, according to Aaron Wright, a blockchain expert at Cardozo Law School.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\"I think the Internet has long offered massive distribution for media, but there has been no monetization scheme that works really well,\" he said, adding that NFTs help fix this shortcoming.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eSpecifically, Wright points out that NFTs finally offer a way for artists to sell digital versions of their work that are scarce and unique. That scarcity means they can not only enjoy a new revenue stream, but also take a cut when the NFT is resoldan arrangement that platforms like the \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60918/winklevoss-nft-marketplace-nifty-gateway-valuation\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eWinklevoss-owned Nifty Gateway\u003c/a\u003e help facilitate.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFrom a broader perspective, Wright says artists' ability to sell NFTs could take some of the rancor out of the copyright debate as the business model of online distribution shifts from trying to sell as many copies as possible to selling fewer items for more money to dedicated fans.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWright is not the only one who sees a shift in how creators are trying to make money from the Internet. In recent weeks, venture capitalists and tech watchers have been sharing an influential essay called \"\u003ca href=\"https://kk.org/thetechnium/1000-true-fans/\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" rel=\"nofollow external noopener\"\u003e1000 true fans\u003c/a\u003e\" in which \u003cem\u003eWired\u003c/em\u003e editor Kevin Kelly predicted that the future of creative industries would revolve artists selling their work to small communities of passionate supporters. The essay is from a decade ago but, with the arrival of NFTs, Kelly's prediction appears to be coming true.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn a related trend, tech writer Will Oremus claims that a growing number of Internet users have grown exhausted with mega-platforms like Facebook that rely on algorithms to show a steady stream of emotional or sensational content. He says they are turning instead to smaller forums like SubStack or Clubhouse where \"Super Fans\" can connect in a more intimate community. If Oremus is correct, the growth of these communities will offer creators new opportunities to make money from the Internetincluding from NFTs.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOf course, such rosy scenarios will depend on NFTs proving they are more than a fad. And many people are skeptical that's the case. Those skeptics include \u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"More about Litecoin\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/crypto-news/litecoin\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eLitecoin\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e creator Charlie Lee, a prominent cryptocurrency entrepreneur, who poured cold water on NFTs last week:\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cblockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\"\u003e\n\u003cp lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"\u003e10/ I will end this thread with this image I found on Reddit. \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIt\u0026#39;s funny because it\u0026#39;s true. What\u0026#39;s the value of an NFT of a song when everyone in the world can own the actual song for $1? \u003ca href=\"https://t.co/jKFY7mxbH6\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003epic.twitter.com/jKFY7mxbH6\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u0026mdash; Charlie Lee [LTC] (@SatoshiLite) \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/SatoshiLite/status/1367570137939726336?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eMarch 4, 2021\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cscript async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"\u003e\u003c/script\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eLee's tweet underscores how the future success of NFTs depends on persuading a critical mass of people that they are worth owning, and that they will keep their value in the future. Doubters may point to the Beanie Babies phenomenon of the 1990s when people paid hundreds or thousands of dollars for $10 stuffed collectibles, only to see the market collapse and never recover.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eOn the other hand, each day in 2021 has brought new evidence that people think NFTs are valuable, and will pay good money to own one.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe latest example? This week, a bidder at Christie's auction house paid $69.3 million to own an \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60971/beeples-nft-artwork-sells-for-60-3-million-in-christies-auction\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eNFT artwork by Beeple\u003c/a\u003e. It was the third biggest sale by a living artist to date.\u003c/p\u003e\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"\u003cp\u003eNFTs are giving rise to new forms of copyright infringement, but could
