e":"Copyright","slug":"copyright","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":13630,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":5,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":212,"name":"cryptocurrency","slug":"cryptocurrency","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":212,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":2550,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":4836,"name":"Gaming","slug":"gaming","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":4836,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":139,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":9400,"name":"Music","slug":"music","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":9400,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":29,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":20731,"name":"NBA","slug":"nba","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":20731,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":27,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":29365,"name":"nfts","slug":"nfts","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":29365,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":62,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}},{"term_id":5423,"name":"Technology","slug":"technology","term_group":0,"term_taxonomy_id":5423,"taxonomy":"post_tag","description":"","parent":0,"count":2103,"filter":"raw","custom_fields":{"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"","focuskw":null,"linkdex":null,"metakeywords":null,"meta-robots-noindex":null,"meta-robots-nofollow":null,"canonical":null,"redirect":null,"opengraph-title":"","opengraph-description":"","opengraph-image":null,"twitter-title":"","twitter-description":"","twitter-image":null},"authors":[]}}],"link":[]},"content_text":"If there was a contest for acronym of the year, \"NFT\" would be the clear favorite for 2021. Short for non-fungible tokens, NFTs are having a moment as fans scramble to \"own\" pieces of digital art or pop culture moments.\n\nWhile many people are baffled by the trend, no one can deny it's been lucrative. In recent weeks, buyers have laid down millions of dollars to acquire NFTs issued by the likes of the artist Beeple and the musician Grimes.\n\nBut along with the money and hype, the NFT craze has spurred a debate over what it means to own digital property, and the role of copyright on the Internet. Some suggest NFTs might soothe long-running tensions between creators and tech platformswhile others point out the trend has already given rise to new forms of piracy and rip-offs.\n\nWHAT EXACTLY ARE PEOPLE BUYING?\n\nNFTs are not new. They've been around since 2017 when a company called Dapper Labs began selling NFTs in the form of unique digital cat cartoons called CryptoKitties. Those kitties were the subject of a short-lived craze, and some sold for tens of thousands of dollars before the fad quickly fizzled. Now, in 2021, NFTs have come roaring back as the phenomenon has expanded well beyond digital cats.\n\nToday, the range of NFTs for sale includes just about anything that can be captured as a digital file. The band Kings of Leon, for instance, dropped NFT versions of their new album, while the NBA is selling NFT basketball highlights. An original work by street artist Banksy has been burned and turned into an NFT. And last week, the bidding for an NFT of Twitter founder Jack Dorsey's first tweet topped $2 million.\n\nAll of this raises the question of _just what are people buying_? After all, any of these NFT artifacts can be easily copiedlegally or otherwiseby anyone with an Internet connection and a basic familiarity with software. Why pay to \"own\" Jack Dorsey's tweet when you can print out or embed the same tweet on a website like I've done below?\n\n\u003ejustsettingupmytwttr\n\u003e\n\u003ejack(@jack)March21,2006\n\nNFT enthusiasts will tell you that the artifact they bought might look (or sound) identical to copies on the Internet, but _their_ version comes with a unique ownership certificate. That certificate is inscribed on a blockchain to create a tamper-proof transaction record to show the world that the artworkor song or sports highlightbelongs to someone. Think of it as a serial number or a signature from the artist.\n\nWhat this means, at least to NFT boosters, is that they own something unique. Just as an original painting signed by a famous artist is worth millions, even though thousands of college students tape the same image to their dorm room, NFT owners claim that their piece of digital art is the \"real\" one.\n\nNonetheless, NFT owners might be surprised to discover that what they \"own\" is rather limited.\n\nAs law professors like to tell their students, property is like a bundle of sticks. Each stick in the bundle represents a right to do something, such as the right to sell the piece of property, or harvest it or destroy it, and so on. This is certainly true of copyright, which contains more sticks in its bundlesuch as the right to broadcast and merchandise an imagethan many people realize.\n\nIn the case of sports leagues and musical acts, lawyers are taking pains to ensure their clients keep most of the ownership sticks in the copyright bundle for themselves. For fans, what they receive when buying an NFT is a license that lets them do little beyond display or transfer the work. Purchasers of NFTs issued by the NBAcalled \"Moments\"can't, for instance, modify the highlight they buy, or display it in a way the league considers hateful or offensive.\n\nSo You Bought an NBA Top Shot NFT. What Do You Actually Own?\nSome of these limits go beyond those that go with owning a physical pack of sports cards. In the case of those physical cardswhich the NBA likes to invoke as a comparison to NFTsthe owner is free to draw mustaches on the players, or glue the card to a controversial collage. This might not be the case with NFTs. One can imagine a situation in which pro-democracy activists use their NFTs to call attention to the NBA's attempts to cozy up to China, and the league responds by deleting the NFTs.\n\nThere are limits to what you can do with a physical card too, of course. Sports leagues' intellectual property rights mean you can't replicate the card images for a t-shirt business, but the rights are certainly broader than what attaches to these NFTs.\n\nA NEW FORM OF PROPERTY BRINGS NEW FORMS OF PIRACY\n\nTonya Evans, an intellectual property scholar at Penn State Dickinson Law, studies blockchains and NFTs and wrote an influential 2018 paper on the CryptoKitties phenomenon. She believes that NFTs offer an important new way for creators to connect and earn money from their fans.\n\nShe notes that a number of Black artists have been at the forefront of the NFT craze, using forums like the new social media audio app Clubhouse to market and sell their works. Evans says that the tech underlying NFT provides a way to counteract the Internet's capacity for endless replication and lets artists prove a digital work is unique.\n\n\"You can code for the integrity of the work,\" said Evans. \"Technology threatened the music industry, letting anyone make a perfect digital copy of the original, and now maybe this is the technology that can cure that.\"\n\nEvans is right that NFT tech offers new opportunities for creators. It's not just prominent artists like Grimes or Beeple that are making real money selling NFTs. So are lesser-known artists, who are using platforms like Nifty Gateway and OpenSea to sell limited edition prints of sneakers and boomboxes. In this sense, NFTs represent a new spigot of money that didn't exist before.\n\nCan NFTs Change How We Value Music?\nBut like everything else on the Internet that makes money, the NFT craze has attracted parasitic bad actors looking to cash in on the works of others. That's what happened to an artist who creates digital pictures under the name Weird Undead. She discovered someone has been stealing her images and selling them as NFTs:\n\n\u003eItriedtoignorewhole#NFThysteriabutWHATTHEFUCK\n\u003eIdon'tgiveanypermission(ESPECIALLYtorandomjerks)tomaketokensfrommycontentandIfeelsoangrypic.twitter.com/E9UKF1AXug\n\u003e\n\u003edon'tgiveup,skeleton(@WeirdUndead)March9,2021\n\nIn the last week, Weird Undead (who asked _Decrypt_ not to use her real name) has been filing a flurry of legal notices with OpenSeaone of the biggest NFT marketswhile her fans have been doing the same so as to stop what she calls \"insane and pointless copyright infringement.\" She has also discovered that copycats have been using a service called Tokenized Tweets to create and sell tweets based on her work, and asked it to stop.\n\nMeanwhile, influential figures in the cryptocurrency industry, including Meltem Demirors of CoinShares and Neeraj Agrawal of Coin Center, have complained of random people repackaging their tweets as tokens for sale:\n\n\u003eitsprettyannoying\n\u003e\n\u003eNeerajK.Agrawal(@NeerajKA)March9,2021\n\nHucksters flogging unauthorized tokens are just one part of the emerging piracy problems surrounding NFTs. A potentially more serious one is the emergence of competing blockchain services, each of which promise that _they_ provide the authoritative record that a given NFT is unique. The situation is akin to a town having two competing services to register land deeds, or two auction houses each claiming they have the legitimate title to a piece of fine art. The issue is potentially an existential one for the nascent NFT industry, which stakes its existence on being able to prove a given token is unique.\n\nSo far, the main NFT marketplaces are cooperating, with each agreeing to recognize a token as unique even when it passes from one forum to another. But that hasn't stopped the users of Binances blockchain from hosting rogue token shops on the network, which not only sold plagiarized works but also clearly mimicked the store names of existing Ethereum-based NFT shopsfor instance \"Binance Punks\" for \"Crypto Punks\" and \"Bashmasks\" for \"Hashmasks.\"\n\nBinance Smart Chain's Musical Beats, Alleged Ethereum Copycat, Shuts Down Days After Launch\nWhile trademark and copyright law provides a remedy for rip-offs, it's likely to prove difficult for artists to find and sue an infringer, since blockchains, by their nature, are designed to be borderless and decentralized. This would explain why some upset by recent behavior on Binance's network resorted to non-legal measures to express their displeasureincluding posting images from the Tiananmen Square massacre on the company's blockchain. (Binance has ties to China).\n\nSuch disputes raise the question of whether NFTs represent just the latest headache for creators trying to make a living from their work. But while NFTs can pose a nuisance, some are optimistic these problems are outweighed by the potential for artists to earn a new form of incomeand that NFTs could reshape how we view copyright and the Internet.\n\nA BREAKTHROUGH IN THE COPYRIGHT DEBATE?\n\nEven since consumers began using it en masse in the mid-1990s, the Internet has proved a mixed blessing for artists, writers, and other creators. On one hand, the web provides an enormous new platform to reach fans and find new audiences. On the other, it's awash with pirates who copy an artist's work and sell it or give it away for nothing. Meanwhile, the giant tech platforms like Amazon and Spotify have come to enjoy virtual monopolies when it comes to selling digital works and, in the view of critics, failed to pay out a fair share to artists.\n\nAll of this has led to two decades of debate about copyright policy. The debate is often bitter with the entertainment industry accusing tech enthusiasts of supporting piracy and robbing artistswhile opponents accuse the industry of lobbying Congress to pass copyright laws that they view as draconian and prone to abuse.\n\nThe rise of NFTs could help transcend this debate, according to Aaron Wright, a blockchain expert at Cardozo Law School.\n\n\"I think the Internet has long offered massive distribution for media, but there has been no monetization scheme that works really well,\" he said, adding that NFTs help fix this shortcoming.\n\nSpecifically, Wright points out that NFTs finally offer a way for artists to sell digital versions of their work that are scarce and unique. That scarcity means they can not only enjoy a new revenue stream, but also take a cut when the NFT is resoldan arrangement that platforms like the Winklevoss-owned Nifty Gateway help facilitate.\n\nFrom a broader perspective, Wright says artists' ability to sell NFTs could take some of the rancor out of the copyright debate as the business model of online distribution shifts from trying to sell as many copies as possible to selling fewer items for more money to dedicated fans.\n\nWright is not the only one who sees a shift in how creators are trying to make money from the Internet. In recent weeks, venture capitalists and tech watchers have been sharing an influential essay called \"1000 true fans\" in which _Wired_ editor Kevin Kelly predicted that the future of creative industries would revolve artists selling their work to small communities of passionate supporters. The essay is from a decade ago but, with the arrival of NFTs, Kelly's prediction appears to be coming true.\n\nIn a related trend, tech writer Will Oremus claims that a growing number of Internet users have grown exhausted with mega-platforms like Facebook that rely on algorithms to show a steady stream of emotional or sensational content. He says they are turning instead to smaller forums like SubStack or Clubhouse where \"Super Fans\" can connect in a more intimate community. If Oremus is correct, the growth of these communities will offer creators new opportunities to make money from the Internetincluding from NFTs.\n\nOf course, such rosy scenarios will depend on NFTs proving they are more than a fad. And many people are skeptical that's the case. Those skeptics include Litecoin creator Charlie Lee, a prominent cryptocurrency entrepreneur, who poured cold water on NFTs last week:\n\n\u003e10/IwillendthisthreadwiththisimageIfoundonReddit.\n\u003e\n\u003eIt'sfunnybecauseit'strue.What'sthevalueofanNFTofasongwheneveryoneintheworldcanowntheactualsongfor$1?pic.twitter.com/jKFY7mxbH6\n\u003e\n\u003eCharlieLee[LTC](@SatoshiLite)March4,2021\n\nLee's tweet underscores how the future success of NFTs depends on persuading a critical mass of people that they are worth owning, and that they will keep their value in the future. Doubters may point to the Beanie Babies phenomenon of the 1990s when people paid hundreds or thousands of dollars for $10 stuffed collectibles, only to see the market collapse and never recover.\n\nOn the other hand, each day in 2021 has brought new evidence that people think NFTs are valuable, and will pay good money to own one.\n\nThe latest example? This week, a bidder at Christie's auction house paid $69.3 million to own an NFT artwork by Beeple. It was the third biggest sale by a living artist to date.\n","read_this_next_post_id":61241,"read_this_next_post_type":"post","social_share_img_url":"https://cdn.decrypt.co/resize/1024/height/512/wp-content/uploads/2021/03/beeple-nft-everydays-christies-gID_7.jpg","featured_image_caption":"This NFT sold for $69 million at Christie's. In this case, it works a little like a deluxe edition or a bundle; the NFT comes packaged with a set of MP3s and an animated version of the cover art, as well as a physical copy of the vinyl.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eThese perks arent nothing, but its tempting to view the whole rollout as a cynical attempt to cash in on the hype around NFTs and get the band widespread media attentionand it certainly did.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eNFTs are everywhere right now, from the \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60391/nba-built-for-top-shot-nft-craze\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eNBA\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e to \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60587/taco-bell-rides-nft-hype-train-with-collectible-digital-tacos\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eTaco Bell\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e, and artists like Grimes, Yaeji, and Toro Y Moi have been testing the waters. Grimes \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/59827/grimes-nfts-crypto-art\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003esold\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e a collection of visual art for over $6 million; 3LAU, an EDM musician, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/59788/musician-3lau-sells-album-in-nft-form-for-11-million\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003emade\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e $11 million by selling an album as 33 individual NFTs; and \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/56925/linkin-parks-mike-shinoda-auctions-first-nft\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eMike Shinoda\u003c/a\u003e of Linkin Park has sold several multimedia pieces through the NFT marketplace Zora. The website \u003c/span\u003e\u003ci\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eXLR8R\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e announced \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://xlr8r.com/news/xlr8r-is-launching-an-nft-marketplace-for-electronic-music/\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" rel=\"nofollow external noopener\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003ea dedicated marketplace\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e for music NFTs earlier this week, and theres a burgeoning cottage industry of NFT auction houses looking to bring these collectibles to the masses.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=59788 data-post-title=\"Musician 3LAU Sells Album for $11 MillionUsing NFTs\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/59788/musician-3lau-sells-album-in-nft-form-for-11-million/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eMusician 3LAU Sells Album for $11 MillionUsing NFTs\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBut behind the early-stage gimmickry is a genuinely intriguing question about the future of artist economies, and the ways we think about how music is owned. The music business has always been about assigning value to something that fundamentally resists precise valuationwhos to say how much our favorite songs are worth?\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eFor the better part of the last decade, the answer has been streaming services like Spotify and Apple Music, which offer access to a vast library of recorded music for relatively low fees. Their implicit pitch: access has replaced ownership. (When was the last time you purchased a song through the iTunes Store?) Its a business model thats responsible for revitalizing the industry; the decline of physical media sales left a massive hole in the market, and streaming services walked right in. Per the Recording Industry Association of Americas most recent \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://www.riaa.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/02/2020-Year-End-Music-Industry-Revenue-Report.pdf\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" rel=\"nofollow external noopener\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eyear-end report\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e, streaming now accounts for 83% of the entire industrys revenue.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"ad-unit\"\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBut small artists are getting squeezed harder than ever. The largest streaming services distribute money through a pro rata model, which rewards artists in proportion to their total market share: if youre only listening to your favorite indie artist, your money is still going to Drake and Billie Eilish, since, according to \u003c/span\u003e\u003ci\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eRolling Stone \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003echart data, 90% of whats streamed on Spotify is music from the top 1% of performers.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eStreaming is a wonderful technology, but because it is dominated by large tech companies, artists, engineers and the like don't have the ability to self-determine value, said Ben Cronin, a member of the \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2021/03/11/magazine/live-music-covid.html\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eUnion of Musicians and Allied Workers\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e. He added that the pro-rata model has ended up gutting a middle class of musicians that cant generate hundreds of millions of streams per month.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eSpotify has decided to pay artists about $.003 per stream, but profits can be less than that. Cronin, whos one half of the electronic duo Gilligan Moss, said his music was streamed 92,000 times in January; he got a check for $8.19.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eHeres a look at whether NFTs have the potential to change how music is valued, and create a new funding source for artists looking to make back some of the money lost to streaming.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cb\u003eWhat are non-fungible tokens?\u003c/b\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eIn finance, assets are fungibile when theyre fully interchangeable. \u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"bitcoin news\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/crypto-news/bitcoin\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eBitcoin\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e is a fungible asset, since each Bitcoin is worth exactly as much as any other. The same goes for dollars, whichthough they can be torn or drawn on or otherwise physically alteredare always worth exactly as much as other dollars.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eThe idea with NFTs is that each one is unique, one of a kind or one of a very limited batch Theyre typically built on the \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/what-is-ethereum-quickly-explained-four-minute-guide\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eEthereum network\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e, and can take the form of anything on the Internet. Visual art and music are common use cases, but more intangible things \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60791/jack-dorsey-first-tweet-nft-africa-relief-charity\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003elike tweets\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e can be tokenized too. An early example was \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/cryptokitties\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eCryptoKitties\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e, a blockchain-based game focused on collecting digital cat NFTs. The closest analog today might be CryptoPunkstiny, pixelated images of unique characters, some of which have \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/57948/ethereum-cryptopunks-are-selling-for-outrageous-sums-of-money\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003esold for millions of dollars\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=57948 data-post-title=\"Ethereum CryptoPunks Are Selling for Outrageous Sums of Money\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/57948/ethereum-cryptopunks-are-selling-for-outrageous-sums-of-money/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eEthereum CryptoPunks Are Selling for Outrageous Sums of Money\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eBut wait, skeptics retort. Why cant I just screenshot the same art? Or stream the Kings of Leon album on Spotify or YouTube? What could possibly justify such high prices for things I can access for free online?\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eThose are fair questions. Consider Nyan Cat, a looped animation of a cat with a pink Pop-Tart for a torso. Its a ubiquitous GIFan artifact from the early-2010s memescape thats become a piece of Internet history. In celebration of its 10th anniversary, Nyan Cat was turned into an NFT and \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://foundation.app/NyanCat/nyan-cat-219\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" rel=\"nofollow external noopener\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eauctioned\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e through an NFT startup called Foundation, where it sold for 300 ETH, or over $500,000.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eNyan Cat is an example of where this is going, Foundation CEO Kayvon Tehranian told \u003c/span\u003e\u003ci\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eDecrypt\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e. Why is something like Nyan Cat going for 300 ETH? Because it's reached that level of stature within the Internet ecosystem. How many people know about that? Hundreds of millions? How many places has that been referenced?\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=59635 data-post-title=\"Where's the Trust in the $150 Million NFT Art Market?\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/59635/wheres-the-trust-in-the-150-million-nft-art-market/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eWhere's the Trust in the $150 Million NFT Art Market?\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eFor Tehranian, NFTs are a way of ascribing value to a category of cultural phenomena that people already want to pay for. What was previously replicable and free is now, all of a sudden, discrete and monetizable.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eI think we're headed for a world in which every piece of media that's uploaded to the Internet will be represented as a token, he said. And so I think there will be many, many, many, many, many, many forms of value created in that process.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eIts a phenomenon that extends well beyond cryptocurrency. Whats valuable about much of contemporary art is less the physical works themselves than the pieces of paper that certify ownership. Its the same reason knockoff Yeezys arent worth anything, even if theyre \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://youtu.be/0ttzxbqgoZE\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003enearly identical\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e to the real thing, or why expensive sports memorabilia comes with a certificate attesting that its really that pitchers signature the fact of authenticity is what youre paying for, beyond the raw materials.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=61036 data-post-title=\"'Bad Luck Brian' Meme Goes Crypto Art, NFT Sells for $36,000\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/61036/bad-luck-brian-nft/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e'Bad Luck Brian' Meme Goes Crypto Art, NFT Sells for $36,000\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eWhat youre really getting with an NFT is a hard and fast certificate of ownership that hypothetically should live forever on a blockchain. Even if you tokenized another Nyan Cat on another platform, it wouldnt be \u003c/span\u003e\u003ci\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003ethe \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003etokenized Nyan Cat.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eThe Grimes and Kings of Leon NFTs were issued in limited editions, which work like prints in the traditional art market; theres more than one of each, but since the supply is always capped, they still work as collectors items.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cb\u003eNew opportunities for artists\u003c/b\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eRather than just turning a song into an NFT and charging for ownership, the producer Jacques Greene went a step further. After exiting what he characterized as an imperfect publishing deal, he sold an NFT called \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://foundation.app/jacquesgreene/promise-640\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" rel=\"nofollow external noopener\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003ePromise\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e on Foundation, representing the publishing rights to a single of the same name. Its not something thats baked into the code of the NFTinstead, it was a promise to write the buyer into the contract.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eGreene explained\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003ethat the last 10-15 years has aggressively told us that music is free and worthless, and that while less invested fans might still want to buy music on Bandcamp or stream on Spotify, NFTs can be a new option for the diehards.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ciframe title=\"Jacques Greene - Promise (NFT)\" src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/521330445?dnt=1\u0026amp;app_id=122963\" width=\"640\" height=\"640\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"autoplay; fullscreen; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen\u003e\u003c/iframe\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eThe direct line to patronage and putting your money where your mouth is, as far as your passions, is kind of cool, he said. The buyer for Greenes single turned out to be Trevor McFedries, whos responsible for the virtual influencer art project \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miquela\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eLil Miquela\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e, and the high bid was nearly $24,000.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eCharles Damga, who founded the venerable indie label UNO NYC and recently took a job at Foundation, told \u003c/span\u003e\u003ci\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eDecrypt\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e that NFTs are a much more democratized funding opportunity for artists. If you ask him, theyre a complement to streaming services as opposed to a replacement.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eI think like NFTs are beautiful in that they put the actual marketplace in the hands of the artists, Damga said. Theres interest here, and there's people that want to reward their artists in a real way.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eWhere streaming services decide exactly how much a song is worth, NFTs are a way for artists to directly monetize what they create. Tehranian hopes NFTs will create new markets for creators that had been previously sharing their work for free online via the existing version of the Internet (sometimes referred to as Web 2.0, as opposed to an eventual crypto-based \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/what-is-web-3\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eWeb 3.0\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e). Instead of uploading it for free to a Web 2.0 platform, mint it as a token, he said. That token can then be directly monetized by you, by a collector. And then as you build out this collector base, you build out a market for yourself and for your work.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eAnd NFT platforms have \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1WJE9kr5PWpIhHygrRBetmokBVpc78RzAddeLSAV878M/edit#gid=0\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003ecommission structures\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e that allow artists to stay tied to their work even after they sell it. On Foundation, the creator of an NFT gets to keep 10% of each subsequent sale on the secondary market. Zora is even more flexible, allowing creators to structure their own \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/David_Rudnick/status/1362225108123856896?s=20\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eroyalty payments\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eA drawback is that those royalties are platform-specific, meaning that if you want to buy and NFT on Zora and resell it on Rarible, the creator isnt getting exactly the same percentage. But the NFT itself will live in your wallet as long as the Ethereum network is up and running; if Zora and Rarible collapse tomorrow, existing NFTs wont go anywhere.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eMat Dryhurst, an artist and technologist who \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://interdependence.fm/\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" rel=\"nofollow external noopener\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003ehosts a podcast\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e on Internet culture with his wife, the composer Holly Herndon, said that blockchain-based systems are light years ahead of streaming when it comes to prioritizing artists, and that NFTs are a way of rejecting platform risk. In contrast to Web 2.0, where a few big companies dominate, the protocols and \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"What are Smart Contracts?\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/smart-contracts\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003esmart contracts\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e of the Web 3.0 era offer a chance to reconsider how value is distributed, and to whom.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eWe've been living in this very docile state for 10 to 12 years where we just take what we're given, he said. Protocol thinking is: What you want to do with these basic elements? and figure out a way to do it. Because if you do, and many will, I think the next 10 years will be very exciting.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eIts definitely more invigorating than just sitting around complaining about Spotify, Greene said. For the first time there's like, wow, something new that feels like there could be something here, and its kind of a nice feeling.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cb\u003eExclusivity, scarcity, and bad art\u003c/b\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eThe flip side of this is an exclusivity problem: Jacques Greene can move an NFT for $24,000 because hes a respected musician with a sizable following, and also because hes embedded in the crypto community online. Foundation is an invite-only platform, and Greene got involved through Damga, with whom hes had a decade-long relationship.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003ePrivilege in the cryptocurrency space is a huge, huge issue in terms of the barrier to entry and the people who are natively in the space, said Damga.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eThose people who are natively in the space have already established aesthetic norms which may deter certain kinds of artists. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eMany of the most popular NFTs tend to feature images of Elon Musk, the Shiba Inu doge meme, and rocket emojis, along with plenty of Bitcoin logos and references to pop culture; theyre usually garish and didactic, pandering to the extremely online ethos of cryptos wealthiest patrons. The digital artist Beeple makes flashy, sensationalist images in this vein (they might remind you of KAWS or Jeff Koons), which have been \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://www.spikeartmagazine.com/articles/downward-spiral-popular-things-dean-kissick\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" rel=\"nofollow external noopener\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003edescribed by \u003cem\u003eSpike Art Magazine\u003c/em\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e as a very boring sort of outsider art, made by nerds for other nerds. He just sold a piece at Christies for\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60971/beeples-nft-artwork-sells-for-60-3-million-in-christies-auction\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e $69 million\u003c/a\u003e; it was the third-highest price ever paid at auction for work by a living artist.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=60971 data-post-title=\"Beeple NFT Artwork Sells for $69.3 Million in Christies Auction\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/60971/beeples-nft-artwork-sells-for-60-3-million-in-christies-auction/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eBeeple NFT Artwork Sells for $69.3 Million in Christies Auction\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eMat Dryhurst suggested that headline-grabbing sales numbers and off-putting, explicitly crypto-themed artworks might not be a good indication of where NFTs are heading, or what they can do for the value of music. For most people, right now, when they see crypto or blockchain and art, likely all they've seen is a Beeple GIF, and people making market memes on Twitter. I can understand why that would be kind of alienating. I'm not all that excited about that aspect of it.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eEven beyond these visual signifiers, theres a danger in thinking about art as a product. The music that Grimes, Kings of Leon, and others have turned into NFTs is usually available to stream for free online, and paying thousands of dollars for a music NFT doesnt preclude anyone else from listeningat least not always. For her first NFT release, Azealia Banks sold a one-of-one audio sex tape to a pseudonymous buyer for $17,000, and hasnt released it elsewhere. As with the Wu-Tang Clans selling the only copy of \u003c/span\u003e\u003ci\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eOnce Upon a Time in Shaolin\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/i\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e to the fraudster Martin Shkreli, its a model premised on exclusion.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=60791 data-post-title=\"Jack Dorsey: Proceeds From Tweet NFT Will Go to Africa Relief Charity\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/60791/jack-dorsey-first-tweet-nft-africa-relief-charity/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eJack Dorsey: Proceeds From Tweet NFT Will Go to Africa Relief Charity\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eAccording to Mat Dryhurst, without guardrails, this sort of gatekeeping is inevitable. The protocols behind NFTs are just tools like any other: theyre neither exploitative nor inherently pro-artist. Its the people behind the keyboard, coding these things into existence, who decide how equitable these systems can be.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eThere's nothing stopping people from using these tools to create a co-op in which all profits are immediately on chain, distributed between everybody involved, said Dryhurst. You can build whatever utopian projects you see fit here, but I just don't think people are even in the habit of thinking about it.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eTo be sure, a certain degree of exclusivity is inherent to the value proposition of NFTs. EulerBeats is a project looking to turn music into a pure investment play, with a set of 27 algorithmically generated audio tracks in the form of NFTs. (Euler Beats is funded by Ethereum studio ConsenSys, which also funds an editorially independent \u003cem\u003eDecrypt.\u003c/em\u003e) For each beat you own, youre entitled to 8% of what it sells for on the secondary market. Billionaire Dallas Mavericks owner Mark Cuban has \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/BanklessHQ/status/1364255520857731072?s=20\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eframed\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e EulerBeats as a great money-making opportunity. But shouldnt the value of music be tied to the music itself, rather than the potential to be flipped for a quick buck?\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cblockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\"\u003e\n\u003cp lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"\u003ei fully respect the view of those who want nothing to do w the space, but the idea of assets on the blockchain isnt going away. there is a small window to try establish some norms or values that might have real value moving forward. doing nothing now lets the predators define it\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u0026mdash;  (@David_Rudnick) \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/David_Rudnick/status/1367146366468767745?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eMarch 3, 2021\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cscript async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"\u003e\u003c/script\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eThis sort of dynamic isnt specific to crypto; it already exists among vinyl resellers, where rare, limited edition presses are considered investments. That its so easily replicated supports Dryhursts idea that when it comes to the crypto ecosystem, were only limited by how big were thinking. The companies that dominate the current version of the Internet have already set their terms, exploitative or not. In the crypto space, theres a chance for artists to drive the conversation about what comes next.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cb\u003eEcological cost\u003c/b\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eSome artists have already written off NFTs entirely, since crypto as an industry is extremely energy-intensive. The Bitcoin networks current annualized electricity consumption is now nearly 130 TWh, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://cbeci.org/\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" rel=\"nofollow external noopener\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eaccording to research\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e from the University of Cambridges Center for Alternative Finance; for context, the entire country of Ukraine \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://www.eia.gov/international/data/world/electricity/electricity-consumption?pd=2\u0026amp;p=0000002\u0026amp;u=0\u0026amp;f=A\u0026amp;v=mapbubble\u0026amp;a=-\u0026amp;i=none\u0026amp;vo=value\u0026amp;t=C\u0026amp;g=00000000000000000000000000000000000000000000000001\u0026amp;l=249-ruvvvvvfvtvnvv1vrvvvvfvvvvvvfvvvou20evvvvvvvvvvnvvvs0008\u0026amp;s=315532800000\u0026amp;e=1546300800000\u0026amp;\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" rel=\"nofollow external noopener\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eused about 129 TWh\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e in 2019.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"More about Ethereum\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/crypto-news/ethereum\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eEthereum\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e, the blockchain most NFTs run on, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://digiconomist.net/ethereum-energy-consumption/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003euses\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e around 26 TWh. But the disparity is more a function of transaction volume than consumption rates: Bitcoin is still cryptos \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60869/anthony-scaramucci-focused-on-bitcoin-big-dog\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003ebig dog\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e, with a market capitalization that exceeds Ethereums by a factor of about five. With greater demand comes greater energy expenditures.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=40099 data-post-title=\"The Truth About Bitcoin's Green New Deal\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/40099/the-truth-about-bitcoins-green-new-deal/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eThe Truth About Bitcoin's Green New Deal\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eCryptos energy problem has to do with something called a \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/concensus\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eproof-of-work\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e consensus mechanism. When you initiate a Bitcoin or Ethereum transaction, theres no single governing body that verifies it and then carries it out (as with a bank). Instead, the transaction is sent out to a network of computers, each of which is tasked with performing a difficult math problem; the first computer to solve the problem gets to verify the transaction in exchange for newly created (or mined) crypto. Its an intentionally resource-intensive process, since the work of solving the math problem is what proves a transaction is legit.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eFacilities known as crypto mines are dedicated entirely to this process, and form the bedrock of the Bitcoin and Ethereum networks. These are essentially just rows of computers and accompanying cooling systems, whose only function is to crunch numbers in the hopes of being rewarded with crypto. Cambridges data suggests over 70% of the computational power behind Bitcoin is coming from China, which is still \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://www.eia.gov/international/analysis/country/CHN\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" rel=\"nofollow external noopener\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eheavily reliant on cheap coal\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eOffsetra, a group that brokers carbon offsets for companies looking to reduce their climate impact, is already working with the NFT marketplaces \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/60271/zora-nft-carbon-offset-ethereum\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eZora\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e and KnownOrigin. You have all these computers that are basically just computing smashing numbers together, securing the network, said Offsetra analyst Drew Bonneau. And you end up having a race to the bottom of energy usage for Bitcoin miners.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://carbon.fyi/learn\" data-wpel-link=\"external\" rel=\"nofollow external noopener\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eCarbon.fyi\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e, Offsetras calculator for the emissions output of individual addresses on the Ethereum blockchain, formed the basis of Cryptoart.wtf, which was a similar tool developed by the researcher \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://memoakten.medium.com/the-unreasonable-ecological-cost-of-cryptoart-2221d3eb2053\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eMemo Akten\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e specifically for NFTs. Akten took the site down on Friday, citing its role in abusement and harassment toward artists experimenting with NFTs.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cblockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\"\u003e\n\u003cp lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\"\u003eI\u0026#39;m thankful \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/memotv?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e@memotv\u003c/a\u003e disabled \u003ca href=\"https://t.co/j7amLQ1u6z\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003ehttps://t.co/j7amLQ1u6z\u003c/a\u003e . I agree 100% we have a responsibility to be critical of businesses, and to fight for systemic change. I disagreed with the focus on artists, but he sparked an important conversation and I hope it leads to change we all want. \u003ca href=\"https://t.co/s4ivL7ri3M\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003epic.twitter.com/s4ivL7ri3M\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u0026mdash; Sterling Crispin  (@sterlingcrispin) \u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/sterlingcrispin/status/1370484588242296835?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eMarch 12, 2021\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\u003c/blockquote\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cscript async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"\u003e\u003c/script\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eIn a post criticizing Grimes, singer-songwriter Lucy Dacus \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/lucydacus/status/1367611019758080001?s=20\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003ewrote\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e that NFTs are destructive and irresponsible, and Jaime Brooks, who records as Default Genders, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://twitter.com/elite_gz/status/1368278892914429952?s=20\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003ehas called\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e NFTs an ecologically wasteful vanity project.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eCharles Damga acknowledged the environmental impact of NFTs, and said he wants to address artists concerns head-on. Its not falling on deaf ears. Were not like the car industry, saying Its not our responsibility, go talk to the gas companies. Its very much an egalitarian, forward-thinking community that youre entering. You decide whether a lack of a voice is louder than a voice thats going to come in and be progressive.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"embedded-post\" data-id=60795 data-post-title=\"ArtStation Rethinks NFT Crypto Art Push After Environmental Backlash\" data-post-type=\"post\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://wp.decrypt.co/60795/artstation-nft-crypto-art-environmental-backlash/\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eArtStation Rethinks NFT Crypto Art Push After Environmental Backlash\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eTheres also a glimmer of hope in the form of \u003cspan class=\"link\"\u003e\u003ca alt=\"What is Ethereum 2.0\" href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/what-is-ethereum-2-0\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eEthereum 2.0\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003ethe networks \u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003elong-awaited shift away from proof-of-work in favor of \u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/61093/ethereum-just-edged-closer-to-proof-of-stake-via-beacon-chain\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003eproof-of-stake\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e, a far less wasteful consensus mechanism. And blockchains like Flow and Wax are already using proof-of-stake. While theres no set timeline for Ethereum to actually make the jump, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://decrypt.co/resources/what-is-ethereum-2-0\" data-wpel-link=\"internal\"\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eprogress is being made slowly but surely\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eUntil that day comes, does the environmental tolland the stigma that can come with itoutweigh the potential benefits for artists considering jumping into NFTs?\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style=\"font-weight: 400;\"\u003eFor me, it very much comes down to like, are you happy with the existing dynamics on Web 2.0?\" Dryhurst said. If youre not, there is a new world being built.\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"\u003cp\u003eStreaming is squeezing small artists; can crypto provide a more equitable future?\u003c/p\u003e\n","protected":false},"author":105,"featured_media":61244,"comment_status":"closed","ping_status":"closed","sticky":false,"template":"","format":"standard","meta":[],"categories":[23622],"tags":[31559,33098,29929,33097,32976,33096,9400,26608,32994,31841,33095,30077],"person":[],"project":[],"language":[28510],"collection":[],"distinction":[],"definition":[],"seo_link":[],"custom_fields":{"field_post_content_sponsor":"","field_post_tldr_title":"In brief","field_post_tldr_content":null,"featured_image_color_id":"1","multimedia":[],"i18n":{"hreflang_items":[{"hreflang":"en","path":"/61241/can-nfts-change-how-we-value-music/"}],"language":{"language_code":"en","locale":"en_US","text_direction":false,"display_name":"English","native_name":"English","different_language":false}},"yoast":{"metatitle":"","metadesc":"Can NFTs change how we value music?
